Qada for Partial Invalidation of Nafl
Ruling that if only part of the nafl is invalidated, only that part is made up

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that only the invalidated part of a nafl prayer requires qada, and explain the two usul that govern it.

Core Idea
In nafl, each pair of rak'ahs is an independent unit; invalidation of one does not affect the others.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario where a person starts a four-rak'ah nafl prayer, completes the first two rak'ahs with tashahhud, and then invalidates the last two. The Hanafi school holds that only the invalidated pair needs to be made up, not the entire prayer. This ruling is built on two key principles: the independence of each pair (shaf') in nafl, and the completion of a pair once tashahhud is performed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a nafl prayer of four rak'ahs. The ruling: if the last two are invalidated, only those two (one shaf') need qada.
The first two are already complete due to sitting for tashahhud.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'صلوة الليل والنهار مثنی مثنی' (night and day prayer is two by two) from Abu Dawood is cited as evidence.
This hadith supports the independence of each pair.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'muthna muthna' (two by two) indicates that each pair is a separate unit; thus invalidation of one pair does not affect the other.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr bi al-muthna yufidu al-ittihad fi al-nawafil.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may require qada of the entire prayer if the intention was for one continuous unit. The Hanafi view relies on the independence of pairs.
Cross-madhhab dispute: Hanafi distinct position.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and consistent with the zahir al-riwayah. The hadith's zanni thubut is not overridden by istihsan here.
Authority weight: zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳) فان صلی اربع ركعات وقعد فى الاوليين ثم افسد الاخريين قضى ركعتين . اگر چار رکعت نفل نماز کی نیت باندھی ۔ پھر دو رکعت پڑھ کر تشہد میں بیٹھا پھر دوسری دو رکعت کو فاسد کر دیا تو دوسری دو رکعت ہی قضا کرے۔ پہلی دو رکعت پوری ہوگئی۔ یہ مسئلہ دو اصول پر مبنی ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ ہر دور کعت الگ الگ شفعہ ہے۔ ایک کے فساد سے دوسرے میں کوئی اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔ دوسرا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ پہلی دورکعت کے بعد تشہد میں بیٹھ گیا تو وہ دونوں رکعتیں پوری ہو گئیں۔ اب صرف سلام باقی ہے۔ اس لئے دوسری دورکعتوں کو فاسد کیا تو اس کو قضا کرے گا۔ البتہ پہلی دورکعتیں پوری ہو گئیں۔ اس پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔ اصول (1) نفل میں دور کعت الگ الگ شفعہ ہیں (۲) ایک کے فساد سے دوسرے پر اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔ حدیث صلوة الليل والنهار مثنی مثنی ( ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۱۲۹۵) سے استدلال کر سکتے ہیں۔
(13) Then if he prays four rak'ahs and sits in the first two, then invalidates the last two, he makes up two rak'ahs. If one intends four rak'ahs of nafl, then prays two rak'ahs and sits for tashahhud, then invalidates the other two rak'ahs, he only makes up the last two rak'ahs. The first two rak'ahs are complete. This case is based on two principles: (1) In nafl, every two rak'ahs are a separate shaf'. The invalidation of one does not affect the other. (2) After the first two rak'ahs, sitting for tashahhud completes those rak'ahs; only the taslim remains. Therefore, if one invalidates the last two, he must make them up. The first two are complete and unaffected. The hadith 'The night and day prayer is two by two' (Abu Dawood no. 1295) can be used as evidence.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed ruling derived from the general principle that each pair (shaf') in nafl prayer is an independent unit. The scenario: a person prays four rak'ahs of nafl, sits for tashahhud after two rak'ahs (which completes that pair), then invalidates the remaining two rak'ahs. Since the first pair is already complete (the sitting after two rak'ahs constitutes the completion of that shaf'), the invalidation only affects the second pair. Therefore, only two rak'ahs (the second shaf') need to be made up. The author emphasizes two usul: the independence of each shaf' and the completion of the first shaf' by sitting. The hadith 'muthna muthna' is cited as evidence.

Key Terms
شفعة (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs considered an independent unit in nafl prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person prays four rak'ahs of nafl, sits for tashahhud after two, then invalidates the last two, how many rak'ahs should he make up?
A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs
C) One rak'ah
D) None, because nafl is voluntary

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, each pair in nafl prayer is an independent unit; invalidation of one pair does not necessitate qada of the other, completed pairs.

Permissibility of Sitting in Nafl Prayer
Ruling that nafl prayer may be performed sitting even if one is able to stand

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing nafl prayer while sitting and explain the evidence and reward reduction.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer sitting is valid but reward is halved; fard prayer sitting without excuse is invalid.

This lesson examines a fundamental distinction in Islamic prayer: the role of standing (qiyam) in obligatory vs. voluntary prayers. While standing is a pillar (rukn) in fard prayers, it is not required in nafl prayers, though it earns greater reward. The source passage presents the ruling and the prophetic hadith that establishes it, along with the practical consequence: sitting in nafl reduces reward but remains valid, whereas sitting in fard without a valid excuse invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
The passage states that nafl prayer may be performed sitting even if one is able to stand. The ruling is 'ja'iz' (permissible) but with reduced reward.
The ruling applies only to nafl; fard has a different ruling.
2
Locate the Dalil
The author cites the hadith of Imran ibn Husain from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sunan al-Tirmidhi, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) distinguishes rewards: standing gets full, sitting gets half, lying down gets half of that.
This is a hadith ahad, but accepted by all schools.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The Prophet did not prohibit sitting; he only stated the reward differential. Hence, the act is permissible. The explicit mention of reward for sitting indicates validity.
The absence of prohibition is key to permissibility.
4
Distinguish Nafl from Fard
The passage explicitly contrasts: for fard prayer, standing is fard (pillar), so sitting without excuse invalidates. For nafl, standing is not obligatory, so sitting is allowed.
This distinction is crucial for correct application.
5
Confirm the Hanafi Position
The Hanafi school holds this ruling as agreed upon (muttafaq alayh) – the mufta bihi is that nafl sitting is permissible. No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is noted.
The ruling is consistent across the madhhab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۴) و يصلى النافلة قاعدا مع القدرة على القيام . نفل نماز کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنے کی قدرت ہے لیکن پھر بھی بیٹھ کر پڑھنا چاہتا ہے تو پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اس کو ثواب آدھا ملے گا۔ اور فرض نماز میں کھڑے ہونے کی قدرت ہو پھر بھی بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھیگا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ فرض نماز میں قیام فرض ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عمران بن حصين قال سألت النبي علي الله عن صلوة الرجل وهو قاعد فقال من صلى قائما فهو افضل ومن صلى قاعدا فله نصف اجر القائم ومن صلى نائما فله نصف الاجر القاعد (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب صلوۃ القاعد ص ۱۵۰، ابواب تقصیر الصلوة نمبر ۱۱۱۶ارترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء ان صلوة القاعد على النصف من صلوۃ القائم ص ۸۵ نمبر ۳۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفل نماز قدرت کے باوجود بیٹھ کر پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اس کو ثواب کھڑے ہونے والے سے آدھا ملے گا۔
(14) And one may pray nafl sitting while able to stand. One can pray nafl sitting even if he has the ability to stand; however, he will receive half the reward. In obligatory prayer, if one is able to stand but prays sitting, his prayer is invalid because standing (qiyam) is fard in obligatory prayers. The hadith: from Imran ibn Husain, he said: I asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about a man praying sitting. He said: 'He who prays standing is more virtuous, and he who prays sitting has half the reward of the standing, and he who prays lying down has half the reward of the sitting.' (Bukhari, chapter on sitting prayer p. 150, chapters on shortening prayer no. 1116; Tirmidhi, chapter on sitting prayer being half of standing prayer p. 85 no. 37). This hadith shows that one may pray nafl sitting even if able to stand, but his reward is half that of the standing person.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that nafl prayer can be performed sitting even when one is capable of standing, but the reward is reduced by half. For obligatory (fard) prayers, standing is a pillar (rukn); thus if one is able to stand but prays sitting, the prayer is invalid. The hadith of Imran ibn Husain is cited as evidence, where the Prophet explicitly distinguishes the rewards: standing gets full reward, sitting gets half, and lying down gets half of that. Therefore, it is permissible but less meritorious to sit in nafl.

Key Terms
قيام (qiyam): Standing during prayer; for fard, it is a pillar; for nafl, it is not required if sitting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on praying nafl sitting when one is able to stand?
A) It is invalid because standing is required
B) It is permissible but reward is half
C) It is forbidden
D) It is equal in reward to standing

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayer performed sitting while able to stand is valid and permissible, but the reward is half that of standing; fard prayer sitting without a valid excuse is invalid because qiyam is a pillar.

Changing Posture in Nafl: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Dispute on whether it is permissible to sit in nafl after starting standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on sitting in nafl after starting standing, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa permits sitting in nafl unconditionally; the Sahibayn require an excuse.

This lesson examines a nuanced difference within the Hanafi school itself: what happens when a person begins a nafl prayer standing and then sits down? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (collectively known as al-Sahibayn), hold differing views. Understanding this dispute helps clarify the role of intention and the binding nature of actions in supererogatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Dispute
The act is sitting down during a nafl prayer after having begun it in the standing posture. The dispute is whether this is permissible without restriction.
2
State Abu Hanifa's Position
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is unconditionally permissible to sit. No special excuse is required.
This is the more lenient view.
3
State the Sahibayn's Position
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, it is not permissible to sit unless there is a valid excuse (e.g., illness, fatigue).
This view considers the initial intention to stand as binding.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, one may sit arbitrarily; under the Sahibayn's view, sitting without excuse would be makruh or require compensation (e.g., sajda sahw).
This difference affects daily practice and fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۵) وان افتتحها... اگر کھڑے ہو کر نفل شروع کی پھر بیٹھ گیا تو جائز ہے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ جائز نہیں ہے مگر عذر ہو تو
(15) And if he begins it standing... If one starts nafl standing and then sits, it is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is not permissible unless there is an excuse.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether one may change from standing to sitting during a nafl prayer after commencing it in a standing posture. Imam Abu Hanifa permits it unconditionally, while the two disciples (Sahibayn) restrict it to cases of genuine excuse. The text is incomplete, but the core issue revolves around whether the initial intention of standing creates a binding obligation to remain standing. The disagreement likely stems from differing views on the level of obligation (wujub) of qiyam in nafl and whether one can deviate from the initial intention.

Key Terms
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two disciples: Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory or voluntary prayer, not obligatory.
عذر (udhr): Valid excuse, such as illness or genuine fatigue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible without any condition
B) It is not permissible at all
C) It is permissible only with a valid excuse
D) It invalidates the prayer

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, there is an internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa permits sitting in nafl after starting standing without an excuse, while the Sahibayn require a valid reason.

Ruling on Breaking the Last Two Rak'ats of Nafl
Explains ruling when one prays four nafl rak'ats then breaks the last two after sitting for tashahhud.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of independent prayer units (shaf') to determine qada obligations when nafl prayer is interrupted.

Core Idea
In nafl prayer, each two rak'ats are an independent unit; breaking one does not affect the other.

The Hanafi school teaches that nafl prayer is structured as separate pairs (shaf'). This lesson examines a specific case: a person prays four rak'ats of nafl, sits after the first two for tashahhud, then invalidates the last two. The response is grounded in two legal principles and a Prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The scenario: one prays four rak'ats of nafl, sits for tashahhud after the first two, then invalidates the last two. The ruling: only the broken pair needs qada; the first two are valid.
This ruling depends on the completion of the first pair through tashahhud.
2
Understand the two principles
Principle 1: In nafl, every two rak'ats are a separate unit (shaf'). Principle 2: The invalidation of one pair does not affect another. The first pair is complete after tashahhud; only salām is pending.
In fard prayer, the entire prayer is invalid if any part is broken.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith 'Salat al-layl wa al-nahar mathna mathna' (night and day prayer is two by two) is cited. The phrase 'mathna mathna' indicates the independent nature of each pair in nafl.
This is a zanni al-thubut hadith, but its meaning is clear.
4
Compare with opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that qada of broken nafl is not required, citing Quran 9:91. The Hanafi school responds that the hadith specifies the structure of nafl, making qada wajib.
The practical difference: Hanafis require qada; Shafi'is do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۳] (۱۳) فان صلی اربع ركعات وقعد فى الاوليين ثم افسد الاخريين قضى ركعتين

یہ مسئلہ دو اصول پر مبنی ہے۔ ایک یہ کہ ہر دور کعت الگ الگ شفعہ ہے۔ ایک کے فساد سے دوسرے میں کوئی اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔ دوسرا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ پہلی دورکعت کے بعد تشہد میں بیٹھ گیا تو وہ دونوں رکعتیں پوری ہو گئیں۔ اب صرف سلام باقی ہے۔ اس لئے دوسری دورکعتوں کو فاسد کیا تو اس کو قضا کرے گا۔ البتہ پہلی دورکعتیں پوری ہو گئیں۔ اس پر کوئی اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔

اصول (1) نفل میں دور کعت الگ الگ شفعہ ہیں (۲) ایک کے فساد سے دوسرے پر اثر نہیں پڑے گا۔ حدیث صلوة الليل والنهار مثنی مثنی ( ابوداؤد شریف نمبر ۱۲۹۵) سے استدلال کر سکتے ہیں۔
[293] (13) If he prays four rak'ats and sits in the first two, then invalidates the last two, he should make up two rak'ats. This issue is based on two principles: (1) Each pair of rak'ats is a separate unit (shaf'). The invalidation of one does not affect the other. (2) When he sits for tashahhud after the first two rak'ats, those two rak'ats are complete; only the salām remains. Therefore, when he invalidates the last two rak'ats, he makes them up. The first two rak'ats are complete and unaffected. Principles: (1) In nafl, every two rak'ats are separate units. (2) Invalidation of one does not affect the other. The hadith "The night and day prayer is in pairs" (Abu Dawood no. 1295) can be cited as evidence.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn with explanatory commentary. The author establishes that in nafl prayer, every two rak'ats form an independent unit. If one prays four rak'ats with the intention of nafl, sits after the first two for tashahhud (completing them), and then invalidates the final two rak'ats, only the invalidated pair requires qada (compensation). The first two rak'ats are valid and do not need to be repeated. The commentary cites the hadith 'Salat al-layl wa al-nahar mathna mathna' (night and day prayer is two by two) to support the principle that nafl rak'ats are independent pairs.

Key Terms
شفعہ (shaf'ah): A pair of rak'ats; an independent unit of two rak'ats in nafl prayer.
قضاء (qada): Compensatory prayer performed to make up for an invalidated or missed part of a prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone prays four rak'ats of nafl, sits for tashahhud after the first two, then invalidates the last two rak'ats, what must they do?
A) Repeat all four rak'ats
B) Make up only the last two rak'ats
C) No qada is required
D) Make up the first two rak'ats

Key Takeaway
In nafl prayer, each pair of rak'ats is an independent unit; breaking one pair does not affect the other, and only the broken pair requires qada.

Permissibility of Praying Nafl While Sitting
Ruling on nafl prayer while sitting with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying nafl while sitting, cite the hadith proof, and differentiate the obligation of standing in fard versus nafl prayer.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer is permitted sitting even if able to stand, but reward is halved; fard requires standing as a pillar.

This lesson addresses a common question: can one pray voluntary prayers while sitting if physically capable of standing? The Hanafi school, based on prophetic practice, allows it but clarifies that the reward is reduced. In contrast, standing in obligatory prayer is a fundamental pillar, and its deliberate omission invalidates the prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is performing nafl (voluntary) prayer while seated, despite being able to stand. The ruling is permissible (mubah), but not equal in reward to standing.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn (ra) recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sunan al-Tirmidhi. The Prophet (saw) was asked about a man praying while sitting.
Hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but accepted for non-obligatory rulings.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's answer specifies reward: standing prayer is best, sitting prayer gives half the reward of standing, lying prayer gives half of sitting. This indicates sitting is permitted (since reward is given) but less virtuous.
The phrase 'falahu nisf ajr al-qa'im' implies permission and reduced merit.
4
Distinguish from fard prayer
For fard (obligatory) prayer, standing (qiyam) is a rukn (pillar). If one is able to stand but deliberately sits, the prayer becomes invalid (fasid). This contrasts with nafl where standing is not obligatory.
The matn explicitly states: 'If one prays fard sitting while able to stand, the prayer becomes invalid because qiyam is fard.'
5
Note the practical consequence
One may choose to sit for nafl even without excuse, but should be aware that the reward is half. For maximum reward, standing is recommended.
This is consistent with the hadith 'afdal' (more excellent) for standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۴] (۱۴) و يصلى النافلة قاعدا مع القدرة على القيام

نفل نماز بیٹھ کر پڑھ سکتا ہے کھڑے ہونے پر قدرت کے باوجود۔ البتہ اس کو ثواب آدھا ملے گا۔ اور فرض نماز میں کھڑے ہونے کی قدرت ہو پھر بھی بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھیگا تو نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ فرض نماز میں قیام فرض ہے۔

حدیث میں ہے عن عمران بن حصين قال سألت النبي علي الله عن صلوة الرجل وهو قاعد فقال من صلى قائما فهو افضل ومن صلى قاعدا فله نصف اجر القائم ومن صلى نائما فله نصف الاجر القاعد (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب صلوۃ القاعد ص ۱۵۰، ابواب تقصیر الصلوة نمبر ۱۱۱۶ارترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء ان صلوة القاعد على النصف من صلوۃ القائم ص ۸۵ نمبر ۳۷)
[294] (14) And one may pray nafl while sitting, despite being able to stand. One can pray nafl sitting even if able to stand; however, his reward will be half. In fard prayer, if one is able to stand and prays sitting, the prayer becomes invalid because standing is obligatory in fard. The hadith: From 'Imran ibn Husayn: I asked the Prophet (peace be upon him) about a man praying while sitting. He said, 'He who prays standing is more excellent; he who prays sitting has half the reward of the standing; he who prays lying has half the reward of the sitting.' (Bukhari, Bab Salat al-Qa'id, p. 150; Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a anna Salat al-Qa'id 'ala al-nisf min Salat al-Qa'im, no. 37)
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn with supporting proof. The author confirms that in nafl prayer, sitting is permissible even when one is physically able to stand. However, the reward is reduced to half of that for standing. In contrast, for fard prayer, standing (qiyam) is a fard obligation; if one deliberately sits without an excuse, the prayer is invalid. The hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn is cited as evidence, showing that the Prophet (SAW) differentiated between standing and sitting in prayer, with the latter having half the reward.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary or supererogatory prayer, not obligatory but highly encouraged.
قیام (qiyam): Standing posture during prayer.
فرض (fard): Obligatory act; omission incurs sin. In prayer, fard refers to the obligatory prayers and their essential components.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on praying nafl while sitting if one can stand?
A) It is haram
B) It is permissible but reward is half
C) It is invalid without excuse
D) It has the same reward as standing

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, nafl prayer may be performed sitting even if one can stand, but the reward is half; for fard prayer, standing is a required pillar and deliberate omission invalidates.

Starting Nafl Standing Then Sitting: Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on nafl prayer posture change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on sitting in nafl after starting standing, and evaluate the proofs to identify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
When you start nafl standing, you may sit — Abu Hanifa allows it, but the Sahibayn require an excuse.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa and his two chief students disagree on whether one who begins a supererogatory prayer standing may later sit down without a valid excuse. The ruling hinges on whether standing in nafl is obligatory or merely recommended, and on the interpretation of prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed ruling
Recognise that the act is starting nafl prayer standing and then sitting. Dispute: is sitting permissible without excuse?
The ruling applies only to nafl (supererogatory) prayers, not fard.
2
Examine Imam Abu Hanifa's proof
He cites the hadith of 'A'ishah where the Prophet stood after sitting, indicating flexibility. The principle: standing is not obligatory in nafl.
The hadith shows that changing posture during nafl is acceptable.
3
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
They cite a different hadith that the Prophet, if he started standing, would bow standing. They use qiyas to a vow (nadhr): once you start standing, it becomes obligatory to continue.
Their proof relies on the idea that starting an act creates an implicit obligation.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa's response: the second hadith merely describes usual practice, not a prohibition. The first hadith explicitly shows the Prophet changing posture, which overrides the mere description.
The commentary notes that the hadith style suggests permission.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's: one may sit without excuse. The practical difference: according to Abu Hanifa, prayer is valid; according to Sahibayn, it is invalid unless there is an excuse.
This dispute has no effect on the prayer's validity in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۵] (۱۵) وان افتتحها قائما ثم قعد جاز عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى و قالا لا يجوز الا من عذر

وجہ امام ابو حنیفہ : پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ نفل میں کھڑا ہونا لازم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے جتنی دیر تک کھڑا رہا کھڑا رہا اور آگے کے کھڑے ہونے کو لازم نہیں کیا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ بیٹھ سکتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة ان رسول الله الله كان يصلى جالسا فيقرأ وهو جالس فاذا بقى من قرأته نحو من ثلثين آية او اربعين آية قام فقرأها وهو قائم ثم ركع ثم سجد يفعل في الركعة الثانية مثل ذلك (بخاری شریف، باب از اصلی قاعدائم صح او و جد خه تیم ما بقی، ص ۱۵۰ نمبر ۱۹ار مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما و قاعد اص ۲۵۲ نمبر ۳۱ ۷ رترندی شریف، باب من تطوع جالسا ص ۸۵ نمبر ۳۷۴) اس حدیث میں آپ نے بیٹھ کر بھی نماز پڑھی اور کھڑے ہو کر بھی جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کھڑے ہو کر شروع کیا تو بیٹھ کر پوری کر سکتا ہے۔

صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ کھڑے ہو کر نفل شروع کیا تو گویا کہ اس نے اپنے اوپر کھڑے ہونے کو لازم کیا تو گویا کہ یہ عمل انذر ہو گئی۔ اس لئے بغیر عذر کے بیٹھنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ قیاس کا تقاضا بھی یہی ہی۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ سالنا عائشة عن صلوة رسول الله الله فقالت كان رسول الله يكثر الصلوة قائما وقاعدا فاذا افتتح الصلوة قائما ركع قائما واذا افتتح الصلوة قاعدا ركع قاعدا (مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما و قاعد اص ۲۵۲ نمبر ۷۳۰ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کھڑے ہو کر نماز شروع کرے تو کھڑے ہو کر ہی رکوع سجدہ کرتے تھے۔ تاہم حدیث کے انداز سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ کھڑا تھا اور بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھی تو جائز ہوگی۔
[295] (15) And if he starts it [nafl] standing then sits, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa (may Allah have mercy on him), but the two [Sahibayn] say it is not permissible except with an excuse. The reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa: It has passed before that standing is not obligatory in nafl. So as long as he stood, he stood, but he is not obligated to continue standing; therefore he may sit. The hadith from 'A'ishah: The Prophet (peace be upon him) would pray sitting and recite sitting, and when about thirty or forty verses remained, he would stand and recite them standing, then bow and prostrate, and do the same in the second rak'ah. (Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi). This hadith shows that he prayed both sitting and standing, meaning that if he started standing, he could complete it sitting.

The Sahibayn say: If he starts nafl standing, it is as if he obligated standing upon himself, making it like a vow (nadhr). Therefore sitting without excuse is not permissible. Qiyas also requires this. The hadith: We asked 'A'ishah about the prayer of the Prophet; she said: 'The Prophet would often pray standing and sitting. If he started prayer standing, he would bow standing; if he started prayer sitting, he would bow sitting.' (Muslim no. 730). This hadith indicates that if he starts standing, he should bow standing. However, the style of the hadith suggests that it is permissible [to change].
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning whether one who starts nafl prayer standing may later sit without a valid excuse. Imam Abu Hanifa permits it, arguing that standing is not obligatory in nafl, so one is not bound to continue standing. He cites the hadith of 'A'ishah where the Prophet would sometimes stand midway after sitting, indicating flexibility. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that it is not permissible without an excuse because starting standing obligates the continuation of standing, akin to a vow (nadhr). They cite a different hadith from 'A'ishah that suggests consistency in posture. The commentary concludes that the hadith style implies permission, siding with Abu Hanifa. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that it is permissible without an excuse, though the Sahibayn's view is based on qiyas.

Key Terms
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
عذر (udhr): A legitimate excuse that permits deviation from the usual practice in prayer, such as illness or hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if someone starts nafl standing and then sits without a valid excuse?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid and sitting is permissible.
C) The prayer is valid only if one recites while sitting.
D) The prayer is invalid unless one performs sajda al-sahw.

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa permits sitting in nafl even without excuse, and this is the mufta bihi position.

Ruling on Nafl Prayer While Traveling on a Mount
Ruling on nafl prayer while traveling: concessions of qibla and gestures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a traveler may pray nafl on a mount, identify the concessions (qibla and gestures) that apply, and distinguish this ruling from the requirements of fard prayer.

Core Idea
Outside the city, nafl on a mount is valid with gestures and without facing the qibla — a concession to encourage abundant worship.

Many assume that all prayers require facing the qibla and full prostration. However, Islamic law grants special facilitations for voluntary prayers during travel. This lesson examines a clear ruling from the Hanafi tradition that allows a traveler outside the built-up area to pray nafl on a mount, using gestures and any direction, based on sound prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is nafl (voluntary) prayer performed by a person who is outside the city (misr) while riding a mount. The ruling is permissible (ja'iz/mubah).
The permissibility is conditional on being outside the built-up area.
2
Identify the concessions granted
Two main concessions: (1) facing the qibla is not required; the rider may pray in the direction the mount faces. (2) Full ruku' and sujud are replaced by gestures (ima) with the head or body.
These concessions apply only to nafl, not to fard.
3
Locate the dalil (evidence)
The author cites a hadith: Jabir ibn 'Abdullah reported that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would pray voluntary prayer while riding, facing other than the qibla.
The hadith is found in Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim, indicating strong authenticity.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (indication)
The Prophet's actual practice (fi'l) of praying nafl on a mount without facing qibla demonstrates permissibility. Since the Prophet did not always face qibla, it shows that qibla is not a condition for nafl in travel.
The Hanafi school uses prophetic action as a source for rulings when there is no contradictory command.
5
Distinguish from fard prayer
For fard prayer, these concessions do not apply if the person is able to dismount. The traveler must face the qibla and perform full ruku' and sujud. The ruling explicitly states: 'For fard, if able, he should dismount.'
The distinction between fard and nafl is crucial: the rigidity of fard is not relaxed for travel convenience.

Source Text

جو شہر سے باہر ہو وہ نفل پڑھ سکتا ہے سواری پر جس جانب بھی متوجہ ہو اشارہ کر کے۔ شہر سے باہر ہو تو نفل نماز سواری پر بیٹھ کر پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ اور سواری قبلہ کی طرف متوجہ نہ ہو تو ظاہر ہے کہ قبلہ کی جانب رخ نہیں کر سکے گا اس لئے قبلہ کی خلاف جانب رخ کر کے بھی نفل نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ نیز سواری پر رکوع وسجدہ بھی پورے طور پر نہیں کر سکے گا تو اشارہ سے رکوع اور سجدہ کرے گا۔ اس کی بھی گنجائش ہے۔

[29] (16) And whoever is outside the city may pray nafl on his mount, facing any direction it faces, with gestures. One who is outside the city may pray nafl while sitting on a mount, facing any direction. If the mount is not facing the qibla, obviously he cannot face the qibla, so he may pray facing other than the qibla. Also, he cannot fully bow and prostrate on the mount, so he will gesture for bowing and prostration. This is permitted. (1) Nafl prayer can be offered at any time; one should pray it abundantly. Therefore, the Shari'ah has given these concessions: even if facing away from qibla, gesturing for ruku' and sujud, and being on a mount, one may still pray nafl. For fard, if able, he should dismount. (2) The hadith: Jabir ibn 'Abdullah informed that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would pray voluntary prayer while riding, facing other than the qibla. (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith shows that praying nafl facing other than qibla is permissible. (3) 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah informed: I saw the Prophet [continues].
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn with supporting evidence. The author permits a traveler outside the city to perform nafl prayer on a mount, even if the mount faces away from the qibla. The concessions include: (a) not facing the qibla, (b) performing ruku' and sujud through gestures (ima) rather than full movements, and (c) staying seated on the mount. These facilitations are granted because nafl prayer is highly encouraged and can be done in any place or time. For fard prayer, however, the traveler must dismount and face the qibla if able. The hadith from Jabir and 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah confirm that the Prophet himself prayed nafl on a mount while traveling, without strict qibla orientation.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city or town; here it refers to the built-up area of a settlement.
إيماء (ima): Gesture made with the head or body to indicate bowing and prostration when full movement is not possible.

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayer during travel outside the city is permitted on a mount with gestures and without facing the qibla; these concessions do not apply to fard prayer.

Sitting in Nafl After Starting Standing: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting in nafl after starting standing and explain the intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
In nafl, standing is not obligatory; you may sit even if you started standing.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute: what happens if you start a voluntary (nafl) prayer standing and then decide to sit? Does the act of standing become binding? Imam Abu Hanifa and his two principal students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), differed on this point. Understanding their proofs and the final relied-upon position will clarify a practical aspect of nafl prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The act is sitting down in a nafl prayer after having started it standing. The dispute is whether this is permissible without an excuse.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa says it is permissible. His proof is the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet stood after sitting, and the principle that standing is not wajib in nafl.
The hadith demonstrates flexibility: starting standing does not obligate remaining standing.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The Sahibayn say it is not permissible without an excuse. They argue that starting standing creates a commitment like a vow, supported by qiyas and a hadith where the Prophet continued standing if he started standing.
Their qiyas views the initial standing as making standing obligatory.
4
Analyse the tarjih (preferred view)
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view. The explicit practice in the hadith overrides qiyas, and the second hadith does not prohibit sitting.
Intra-Hanafi tarjih often follows the Imam when a clear dalil is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قائما ثم قعد جاز عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى و قالا لا يجوز الا من عذر [۲۹] (١٦) (۱) وجہ امام ابو حنیفہ : پہلے گزر چکا ہے کہ نفل میں کھڑا ہونا لازم نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے جتنی دیر تک کھڑا رہا کھڑا رہا اور آگے کے کھڑے ہونے کو لازم نہیں کیا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ بیٹھ سکتا ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن عائشة ان رسول الله الله كان يصلى جالسا فيقرأ وهو جالس فاذا بقى من قرأته نحو من ثلثين آية او اربعين آية قام فقرأها وهو قائم ثم ركع ثم سجد يفعل في الركعة الثانية مثل ذلك (الف) (بخاری شریف، باب [؟] ، ص ۱۵۰ نمبر ۱۹[؟] مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما و قاعدا ص ۲۵۲ نمبر ۳۱[؟] ترمذی شریف، باب من تطوع جالسا ص ۸۵ نمبر ۳۷۴) اس حدیث میں آپ نے بیٹھ کر بھی نماز پڑھی اور کھڑے ہو کر بھی جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کھڑے ہو کر شروع کیا تو بیٹھ کر پوری کر سکتا ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ کھڑے ہو کر نفل شروع کیا تو گویا کہ اس نے اپنے اوپر کھڑے ہونے کو لازم کیا تو گویا کہ یہ عمل نذر ہو گئی۔ اس لئے بغیر عذر کے بیٹھنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ قیاس کا تقاضا بھی یہی ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ سالنا عائشة عن صلوة رسول الله الله فقالت كان رسول الله يكثر الصلوة قائما وقاعدا فاذا افتتح الصلوة قائما ركع قائما واذا افتتح الصلوة قاعدا ركع قاعدا (مسلم شریف، باب جواز النافلة قائما و قاعدا ص ۲۵۲ نمبر ۷۳۰ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کھڑے ہو کر نماز شروع کرے تو کھڑے ہو کر ہی رکوع سجدہ کرتے تھے۔ تاہم حدیث کے انداز سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ کھڑا تھا اور بیٹھ کر نماز پڑھی تو جائز ہوگی۔
He stood then sat: it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and they (the two) said it is not permissible except with an excuse. (1) The reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa: It has already passed that standing is not obligatory in nafl. Therefore, as long as he stood he stood, and he did not make the remaining standing obligatory. Therefore he may sit. (2) There is a hadith from Aisha that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, would pray sitting and recite while sitting, and when about thirty or forty verses remained from his recitation, he would stand and recite them while standing, then bow, then prostrate, and do likewise in the second rak'ah. (From Bukhari, Muslim, Tirmidhi) This hadith shows that he prayed both sitting and standing, meaning that if one starts standing, he can complete sitting. The two companions (Sahibayn) say: If one starts nafl standing, it is as if he made standing obligatory upon himself, so it becomes like a vow. Therefore sitting without excuse is not permissible. Qiyas also requires this. There is a hadith: We asked Aisha about the prayer of the Messenger of Allah, and she said: The Messenger of Allah often prayed standing and sitting, and when he started prayer standing, he would bow standing, and when he started prayer sitting, he would bow sitting. (Muslim) This hadith indicates that if he starts standing, he bows standing. However, from the style of the hadith it appears that if he started standing and then sat, it would be permissible.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of sitting down during a voluntary (nafl) prayer after having started it standing. The core issue is whether the act of standing, once initiated, becomes binding. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that standing is not a required element (rukn) in nafl, so one may sit without any excuse. He cites the hadith of Aisha (RA) where the Prophet (SAW) would sometimes stand and then sit during his nafl prayer. The two pupils (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) argue that starting the prayer standing creates a commitment akin to a vow (nadhr), making it impermissible to sit without a valid excuse. They support their view with qiyas (analogy) and another hadith where the Prophet (SAW) would continue standing if he started standing. The commentary then favors Abu Hanifa's view, concluding that the hadith style indicates permissibility. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa, allowing one to sit in nafl without excuse.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary supererogatory prayer
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani
قائم (qa'im): Standing position in prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the ruling on sitting in nafl prayer after starting standing without an excuse?
A) Not permissible
B) Permissible
C) Only permissible if in travel
D) Permissible but disliked

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, one may sit in nafl prayer even after starting standing, according to the relied-upon view of Abu Hanifa.

Nafl Prayer on a Mount: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Evidence
Ruling on nafl prayer on a mount outside the city.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying nafl on a mount and identify the hadith evidence supporting the condition of being outside the city.

Core Idea
Outside the city, nafl on a mount with gestures is permissible; inside, dismount and face qibla.

This passage establishes the basic ruling for voluntary prayer on a mount. Using hadith from Jabir and 'Amir ibn Rabi'a, it shows the Prophet's practice. However, the Hanafi school qualifies this with the condition of being outside the city, based on the practice of Ibn 'Umar and specific reports. Understanding this ruling helps avoid performing nafl incorrectly inside city limits.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its permissibility
The act is voluntary (nafl) prayer performed on a mount while traveling. The basic ruling is permissibility, as hadith show the Prophet did so.
This is a concession for travel.
2
List the hadith evidence
Two main hadith: Jabir reported the Prophet prayed nafl while riding not facing qibla; 'Amir ibn Rabi'a saw the Prophet gesturing with his head on a mount. These show permissibility.
Both hadith are in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Determine the condition from the hadith
From the practice of 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar and other reports, the Hanafi school derives that this concession is only outside the city. Inside the city, one must dismount.
The condition is debated (see lesson 2).
4
Note the distinction between nafl and fard
For fard prayer, one must dismount and face qibla with full postures if able. The concession is only for nafl.
This is a key principle in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن كان خارج المصر يتنفل على دابته الى اى جهة توجهت يأمى ايماء. (۱) وجہ: نفل نماز ہر وقت پڑھ سکتا ہے اس کو زیادہ سے زیادہ پڑھے اس لئے یہ تمام سہولتیں شریعت نے دی ہے کہ خلاف قبلہ ہو، رکوع اور سجدہ کا اشارہ ہو۔ سواری پر ہو تب بھی نفل نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ فرض کے لئے قدرت ہو تو سواری سے اترے گا (۲) حدیث میں ہے جابر بن عبد الله اخبره ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلي التطوع وهو راكب في غير القبلة (ب) (بخاری شریف، باب صلوۃ التطوع علی الدواب حيثما توجهت ص ۱۴۸ نمبر ۱۰۹۴، مسلم شریف، باب جواز صلوۃ النافلة على الدابة في السفر حيث توجهت ص ۲۴۴ نمبر ۷۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قبلہ کے رخ کے خلاف نفل نماز پڑھ لے تب بھی جائز ہوگی (۳) عامر بن ربيعة اخبره قال رأيت النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على الراحلة يسبح يؤمى برأسه قبل الى اى وجه توجه ولم يكن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصنع ذلك في الصلوة المكتوبة (الف) (بخاری شریف، باب مینزل للمتو به ص ۱۴۸ نمبر ۱۰۹۷، مسلم شریف، باب جواز صلوة النافلة على الدابة في السفر حيث توجهت ص ۲۴۴ نمبر ۷۰۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفل نماز میں سواری پر رکوع سجدے کا اشارہ کرے گا۔ اور فرض نماز میں اتر کر نماز پڑھنا ہوگی۔ شہر سے باہر کی قید اس لئے لگائی کہ بعض حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے شہر سے باہر نفل کی نماز سواری پر پڑھی تو قبلہ کے خلاف رخ پر پڑھی ہے۔ اس لئے حنفیہ نے قید لگائی کہ شہر سے باہر ایسا کر سکتا ہے۔ شہر میں سواری سے اتر کر نماز پڑھنی ہوگی۔ حدیث میں ہے کان عبد الله بن عمر يصلي في السفر على راحلته اینما توجهت به يؤمى وذكر عبد الله ان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يفعله (ب) (بخاری شریف، باب الایماء علی الدابته ص ۱۴۸ ابواب تقصیر الصلوۃ نمبر ۱۰۹۶، مسلم شریف، باب جواز صلوة النافلة على الدابة في السفر ص ۲۴۴ نمبر ۷۷۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر سفر میں قبلہ کے خلاف رخ پر نماز پڑھتے تھے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ شہر میں ایسا کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ نا امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اوپر کی بہت سے احادیث میں سفر کی قید اور شہر سے باہر کی قید نہیں ہے اس لئے شہر کے اندر سواری پر سوار ہو تو وہاں بھی خلاف قبلہ نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے حضور کو دیکھا کہ آپ سواری پر نفل پڑھ رہے تھے اور سرسے اس جانب اشارہ کر رہے تھے جس جانب متوجہ تھے۔ اور حضور یہ فرض نماز میں نہیں کرتے (ب) حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر سفر میں سواری پر نماز پڑھتے جس طرف سواری متوجہ ہوتی اور اشارہ کرتے۔ اور عبد اللہ بن عمر رضی اللہ عنہما کرتے ہیں کہ حضور ایسا ہی کیا کرتے تھے۔
And whoever is outside the city may perform voluntary prayer on his mount facing whatever direction it faces, gesturing with an indication. (1) Reasoning: Voluntary prayer can be performed at any time; one should perform as much as possible, so the Shariah has given all these facilities: even if facing non-qibla, even if bowing and prostration are by gesture, even if on a mount. For obligatory prayer, if able, he should dismount. (2) There is a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to pray voluntary prayer while riding, not facing the qibla. This hadith shows that it is permissible to pray voluntary prayer facing non-qibla. (3) There is a hadith from 'Amir ibn Rabi'ah that he saw the Prophet, peace be upon him, on a mount glorifying Allah and gesturing with his head towards whatever direction he faced, and the Prophet did not do that in the obligatory prayer. This hadith shows that one will gesture for bowing and prostration in voluntary prayer on a mount. And for obligatory prayer, one must dismount and pray. The condition of being outside the city is imposed because some hadith state that the Prophet prayed voluntary prayer outside the city on a mount facing non-qibla. Therefore, the Hanafis imposed the condition that one may do so outside the city. Inside the city, one must dismount and pray. There is a hadith that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar used to pray in travel on his mount facing whichever direction it faced, gesturing, and he mentioned that the Prophet used to do that. This hadith shows that 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar prayed in travel facing non-qibla, meaning that doing so inside the city is not permissible. Then Imam Abu Yusuf says that many of the above hadiths do not have the condition of travel or being outside the city, so if one mounts inside the city, he may also pray facing non-qibla. Footnote: (a) 'I saw the Prophet performing voluntary prayer on a mount and gesturing with his head towards the direction he was facing, and he did not do that in obligatory prayer.' (b) ''Abdullah ibn 'Umar would pray in travel on his mount facing whichever direction it faced and gesture. And 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar narrated that the Prophet used to do likewise.'
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling for a person outside the city limits to perform voluntary (nafl) prayer on his mount, facing any direction, and making gestures (ima') for bowing and prostration. The basic ruling is that this is permissible, based on multiple hadiths showing the Prophet (SAW) and the Companions doing so during travel. The condition of being outside the city is derived from specific hadiths where the Prophet (SAW) performed such prayer outside Medina. Therefore, the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) restricts this concession to outside the city. Inside the city, one must dismount and pray facing the qibla with proper postures. However, Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees, arguing that the hadiths do not carry this restriction, so the concession applies even within the city. The commentary presents Abu Yusuf's view but the relied-upon position is the one with the condition of being outside the city.

Key Terms
سواری (sawari): A riding animal (mount)
اشارہ (isharah): Gesture made with the head for bowing and prostration when unable to do full movements on a mount
شہر سے باہر (shahr se bahar): Outside the city limits (beyond the built-up area)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for praying nafl on a mount with gestures in the Hanafi school?
A) One must be inside the city
B) One must be outside the city
C) It is allowed anywhere
D) It is only allowed during Hajj

Key Takeaway
Hanafi school permits nafl on a mount outside the city with gestures; inside, one must dismount and face qibla.

The Condition of Being Outside the City: Abu Yusuf's Contrary View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the condition of being outside the city.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain Abu Yusuf's position in the intra-Hanafi dispute and the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) for this ruling.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf permits nafl on a mount even inside the city; the majority requires outside.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani condition the concession on being outside the city, while Abu Yusuf sees the hadith as unconditional. Understanding this dispute clarifies the operative ruling for fatwa and highlights how the Hanafi school weighs evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad require that the person be outside the city limits. Inside the city, one must dismount.
This is the position of Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Identify Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues that the hadith do not carry the condition of being outside the city, so the concession applies generally.
He relies on the apparent generality of the texts.
3
Compare the dalil of both sides
The majority cites hadith where the Prophet prayed outside Medina and the practice of Ibn 'Umar restricting it to travel. Abu Yusuf points to the general permission.
The dispute is over how to harmonize the hadith.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: inside the city, the majority says not permissible; Abu Yusuf says permissible.
Mufti must know which view is relied upon.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The majority position is mufta bihi (operative). Abu Yusuf's view is considered a weaker, minority opinion within the school.
Tarjih is based on the stronger evidence.

Praying on a Riding Animal: Nafl vs Fard
Ruling with proof on nafl vs fard on a riding animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying supererogatory and obligatory prayers on a riding animal, and identify the condition of being outside the city.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer on a mount is allowed with gestures outside the city; fard requires dismounting and facing Qibla.

Can you pray while riding a camel, car, or train? The answer depends on whether the prayer is obligatory or voluntary. The Hanafi school derived a clear distinction from the Sunnah of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and the practice of the Companion Abdullah ibn Umar. This lesson unpacks the proof and the condition that limits this concession to outside the city.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being discussed: prayer on a riding animal. Distinguish between supererogatory (nafl) and obligatory (fard) prayers.
The hadith explicitly mentions the Prophet's practice for nafl and his omitting it for fard.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence cited: the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim. Understand that it is a sunnah ahad with zanni thubut but qati dalalah.
The words 'يُؤمِي بِرَأسِهِ' and 'لَمْ يَصْنَعْ ذَلِكَ فِي الصَّلَوَةِ المَكْتُوبَة' are key.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the hadith proves the ruling: the Prophet gestured in nafl but did not in fard, indicating a clear distinction.
This is a direct textual indication (nass) of the difference.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement: Abu Yusuf permits nafl on a mount even inside the city, as many hadiths do not mention the condition of travel.
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) follows Abu Hanifa's restriction to outside the city.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the restriction is preferred: because the hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar explicitly mentions 'in travel', and the Hanafi jurists consider this a necessary condition for the concession.
Tarjih authority: Al-Hidayah and later works side with Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشرح الثميرى الجزء الأوّل
۲۰۳
كتاب الصلوة
على الراحلة يسبح يؤمى برأسه قبل الى اى وجه توجه ولم يكن رسول الله الله الله يصنع ذلك في الصلوة المكتوبة (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب مینزل للمتو به ص ۱۴۸ نمبر ۱۰۹۷ر مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوة النافلة على الدابة في السفر حيث تو جھت ص ۲۴۴
نمبر ۷۰۰ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نفل نماز میں سواری پر رکوع سجدے کا اشارہ کرے گا۔ اور فرض نماز میں اتر کر نماز پڑھنا ہوگی۔ شہر سے باہر کی قید اس لئے لگائی کہ بعض حدیث میں ہے کہ آپ نے شہر سے باہر نفل کی نماز سواری پر پڑھی تو قبلہ کے خلاف رخ پر پڑھی ہے۔اس لئے حنفیہ نے قید لگائی کہ شہر سے باہر ایسا کر سکتا ہے۔ شہر میں سواری سے اتر کر نماز پڑھنی ہوگی۔ حدیث میں ہے کان عبد الله بن عمر يصلي في السفر على راحلته اینما توجهت به يؤمى وذكر عبد الله ان النبى الله كان يفعله (ب) ( بخاری شریف ، باب الایماء علی الدابته ص ۱۴۸ ابواب تقصیر الصلوۃ نمبر ۱۰۹۶ر مسلم شریف ، باب جواز صلوة النافلة على الدابة في السفر ص ۲۴۴ نمبر ۱۶۱۴/۷۷۰) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر سفر میں قبلہ کے خلاف رخ پر نماز پڑھتے تھے۔ جس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ شہر میں ایسا کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔
نا امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ اوپر کی بہت سے احادیث میں سفر کی قید اور شہر سے باہر کی قید نہیں ہے اس لئے شہر کے اندر سواری پر سوار ہو تو وہاں بھی خلاف قبلہ نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) میں نے حضور کو دیکھا کہ آپ سواری پر نفل پڑھ رہے تھے اور سرسے اس جانب اشارہ کر رہے تھے جس جانب متوجہ تھے۔ اور حضور یہ فرض نماز میں نہیں کرتے (ب) حضرت عبد اللہ بن عمر شفر میں سواری پر نماز پڑھتے جس طرف سواری متوجہ ہوتی اور اشارہ کرتے۔ اور عبد اللہ بن عمرڈ کر کرتے ہیں کہ حضور ایسا ہی کیا کرتے تھے۔
On the riding animal, he glorifies and gestures with his head towards wherever he faces, and the Messenger of Allah did not do that in the obligatory prayer (a). From this hadith it is understood that in supererogatory prayer one will gesture for bowing and prostration while on the mount, and for obligatory prayer one must dismount and pray. The condition of being outside the city is added because in some hadith, he prayed supererogatory prayer on a mount outside the city facing opposite of qibla. Therefore, the Hanafis stipulated that this is permissible outside the city. In the city, one must dismount and pray. In a hadith, Abdullah ibn Umar used to pray in travel on his mount whichever direction it faced, gesturing, and Abdullah mentioned that the Prophet did that (b). From this hadith it is understood that Abdullah ibn Umar prayed in travel facing non-qibla. This means that doing so in the city is not permissible. Imam Abu Yusuf says that in many of the above hadiths, there is no condition of travel or being outside the city, so if one is mounted inside the city, he can also pray facing non-qibla there. Footnote: (a) I saw the Prophet praying supererogatory on a mount and gesturing with his head towards whichever direction he faced, and he did not do this in obligatory prayer. (b) Abdullah ibn Umar would pray on a mount in travel facing whichever direction the mount faced, gesturing, and Abdullah reports that the Prophet used to do this.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) concerning prayer on a riding animal, distinguishing between supererogatory (nafl) and obligatory (fard) prayers. The author begins with a hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim showing that the Prophet would gesture with his head in supererogatory prayer while mounted. This proves that for nafl, gestures suffice and one need not face the qibla. For fard, explicit hadith states that the Prophet did not do this; therefore, one must dismount and pray facing the qibla. The author then explains that the Hanafi school adds the condition that this concession is only outside the city, based on a hadith that Abdullah ibn Umar prayed in travel on his mount facing non-qibla. Thus within the city, one must dismount. Finally, a note from Imam Abu Yusuf is presented: he holds that since many hadiths do not mention the condition of travel or being outside the city, one may also pray nafl on a mount inside the city facing any direction. This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa (and the relied-upon position) restricts it to outside the city, while Abu Yusuf permits it even inside. The footnote provides the exact wording of the hadiths for reference.

Key Terms
الراحلة (al-rahilah): A riding animal (camel, mount) used for travel.
إيماء (ima'): Gesturing with the head to indicate ruku' and sujud instead of full bending.
النافلة (al-nafilah): Supererogatory prayer, voluntary.
المكتوبة (al-maktubah): The obligatory prayer (fard).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, which prayer can be performed on a riding animal with gestures facing any direction?
A) Fard prayer, but only outside the city
B) Nafl prayer, but only outside the city
C) Nafl prayer, both inside and outside the city
D) Fard prayer, both inside and outside the city

Key Takeaway
Nafl prayer on a mount with gestures is permissible only outside the city; fard requires dismounting and facing qibla.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Sajdah al-Sahw: When and How to Compensate for Forgetfulness in Prayer
Ruling and method of prostration of forgetfulness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (wajib) of sajdah al-sahw, identify the cases that trigger it (increase or decrease in wajib or fard acts), and describe the correct Hanafi method of performing it.

Core Idea
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib to repair an unintentional increase or decrease in wajib or repeated fard acts, not for missing a sunnah.

Prayer is a precise act of worship, but human forgetfulness is inevitable. The Shariah has provided a beautiful mechanism to repair minor errors: the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw). Understanding when this prostration is required and how to perform it correctly according to the Hanafi school ensures your prayer remains valid and complete without unnecessary repetition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggers
Sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib when there is an unintentional increase (e.g., an extra rak'ah) or decrease (e.g., forgetting the first tashahhud) in the prayer, provided the change involves a wajib act or repetition of a fard act. Leaving a sunnah does not trigger it.
A fard missed entirely invalidates the prayer; sajdah al-sahw cannot fix that.
2
Examine the hadith for decrease
The hadith of Imran ibn Husayn (RA) shows the Prophet (PBUH) forgot a rak'ah in Asr, completed it, then gave salam, performed sajdah al-sahw, and gave salam again. This establishes the method for deficiency.
The salam before sajdah is key: the sajdah comes after the final salam, not before.
3
Examine the hadith for increase
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA) narrates that the Prophet (PBUH) prayed five rak'ah for Zuhr, was reminded, and performed sajdah al-sahw without repeating the entire prayer. This shows that an extra rak'ah is compensated by sajdah, not by repeating the prayer.
The Prophet did not add another rak'ah to correct the increase; sajdah sufficed.
4
Learn the Hanafi method
According to the Hanafi school, the correct sequence is: after the final salam (to the right), perform two prostrations, then recite tashahhud, send blessings, supplicate, and finally give salam to both sides. This is based on the practice of the Prophet (PBUH) in the hadith of deficiency.
Some schools differ on timing; Hanafis emphasize sajdah after salam.
5
Distinguish from other schools
The Shafi'i school holds sajdah al-sahw as sunnah (not wajib) and typically performs it before the final salam. The practical difference is whether the prayer is considered incomplete if sajdah is omitted voluntarily.
Hanafis consider leaving sajdah al-sahw intentionally as sinful, requiring prayer repetition.

ضروری نوٹ سجود السهو : کوئی واجب بھول جائے یا واجب کی زیادتی ہو جائے یا فرائض مکرر ادا ہو جائیں تو اس کو گویا کہ پورا کرنے کے لئے سجدہ سہو واجب ہے۔ سنت کے چھوڑنے سے سجدہ سہو نہیں ہے۔ فرض چھوٹ جائے تو نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عمران بن حصين ن قال سلم رسول الله الله الله في ثلاث ركعات من العصر ثم قام فدخل الحجرة فقام رجل بسيط اليدين فقال اقصرت الصلوة يا رسول الله فخرج مغضبا فصلى الركعة التى كان ترك ثم سلم ثم سجد سجدتی السهو ثم سلم (الف ) ( مسلم شریف، باب فصل من ترک الرکعتین اونحوهما فلیتم مابقی و یسجد سجدتین بعد التسلیم ،ص۲۱۴، نمبر ۱۲۹۴٫۵۷۴؎ بخاری شریف ، باب هل یا خذ الا ام از اشک بقول الناس ،ص ۹۹ نمبر ۷۱۴ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الامام نبض فی الرکعتین ناسیا بص ۸۳ نمبر ۳۶۴ را بو داؤد شریف، باب السهو فی السجدتین، ص۱۵۳، نمبر ۱۰۱۸ اس باب کی آخری حدیث ہے ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی واجب بھول جائے تو سلام کرے پھر سجدہ سہو کرے پھر سلام پھیرے۔ [۲۹۷] (۱) سجدہ سہو واجب ہے۔ واجبات کے زیادہ کر دینے میں یا کم کر دینے میں ۔ سلام کے بعد دو سجدے کرے پھر تشہد پڑھے اور سلام کرے۔
نتشر نماز میں واجب کی کمی رہ جائے یا زیادتی ہو جائے یا خلاف ترتیب ہو جائے تو اس کو پورا کرنے کے لئے سجدہ سہو کرنے گا ۔ اور سلام پھیرے گا۔ حفیہ کے نزدیک تشہد پڑھ کر دائیں جانب ایک سلام کرے پھر دو سجدہ سہو کرے پھر دوبارہ تشہد پڑھے، درود پڑھے، دعا پڑھے اور دوبارہ دونوں جانب سلام کرے۔ (1) اوپر کی حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے کہ آپ نے کمی زیادتی میں سلام کیا ہے پھر سجدہ سہو کیا ہے اور پھر دوبارہ سلام کیا ہے۔ زیادہ ہونے پر سجدہ سہو کیا ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله قال صلى النبي الله الظهر خمسا فقالوا ازيد في الصلوة؟ قال وما ذاك قالوا صليت خمسا قال فتى رجله وسجد سجدتین (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب ما جاء فی القبلة ومن مر الا عادة على من سی ص ۵۸ نمبر ۴۰۴ ر مسلم شریف ، باب من مصلی شما الانجوه ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں پانچ رکعت پڑھنے پر آپ نے سجدہ سہو کیا ہے جو زیادہ کرنے پر سجدہ سہو ہوا۔ کمی پر سجدہ سہو کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله بن بحينة انه قال صلى لنا رسول الله الله ركعتين
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے عصر کی تین رکعت میں سلام کر لیا۔ پھر کھڑے ہو گئے اور کمرے میں داخل ہوئے۔ پھر ایک آدمی کھڑا ہوا جسکے ہاتھ لمبے تھے تو پوچھایا رسول اللہ کی کیا نماز میں کمی ہوگئی ؟ تو آپ گفصہ میں نکلے اور وہ رکعت پڑھائی جو چھوٹ گئی تھی پھر سلام کیا پھر سجدہ سہو کیا پھر سلام کیا (ب) آپ نے ظہر کی پانچ رکعت پڑھائی تو لوگوں نے کہا کیا نماز میں زیادتی ہوگئی؟ تو آپ نے فرمایا یہ کیا بات ہے؟ لوگوں نے کہا آپ نے پانچ رکعتیں پڑھی ہیں۔ راوی کہتے ہیں آپ نے پاؤں موڑا اور دو سجدے کئے۔
Chapter of Sajdah al-Sahw. [297](1) Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib in increase and decrease. After the salam, he performs two prostrations then [recites tashahhud and salam]. Necessary note: Sajdah al-Sahw: if one forgets a wajib, or increases a wajib, or repeats fard acts, then to complete it, sajdah al-sahw is wajib. Leaving a sunnah does not require sajdah al-sahw. If a fard is missed, the prayer becomes invalid. The proof is the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn: The Messenger of Allah gave salam after three rak'at of Asr, then stood and entered his chamber. A man with long hands stood and said, 'Has the prayer been shortened, O Messenger of Allah?' He came out angry, prayed the rak'ah he had missed, then gave salam, then performed two prostrations of forgetfulness, then gave salam. From this hadith it is understood that if one forgets a wajib, he should give salam, then perform sajdah al-sahw, then give salam again. [297](1) Sajdah al-Sahw is wajib. In increasing or decreasing wajibat. After salam, he performs two prostrations, then recites tashahhud, and gives salam. If a wajib is left incomplete or increased or done in wrong order, then to complete it he will perform sajdah al-sahw and give salam. According to the Hanafis, he recites tashahhud, gives salam to the right once, then performs two sajdah al-sahw, then recites tashahhud again, sends blessings, supplicates, and then gives salam to both sides. (1) The above hadith proves that he gave salam after a deficiency/increase, performed sajdah al-sahw, then gave salam again. The proof for increase is the hadith of Abdullah: The Prophet prayed Zuhr five rak'at; they said, 'Has the prayer been increased?' He said, 'What is that?' They said, 'You prayed five.' He then turned his foot and performed two prostrations. In this hadith, on praying five rak'at, he performed sajdah al-sahw, which was due to increase. The proof for decrease is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhaynah: He said, 'The Messenger of Allah led us in two rak'at...' Footnote: (a) The Prophet gave salam after three rak'at of Asr, then stood and entered his room. Then a man with long hands stood and asked, 'O Messenger of Allah, has the prayer been shortened?' He came out angry and prayed the rak'ah that had been missed, then gave salam, then performed sajdah al-sahw, then gave salam. (b) He prayed Zuhr five rak'at; they asked if the prayer was increased. He said, 'What is that?' They said, 'You prayed five.' The narrator says he turned his foot and performed two prostrations.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) for the prostration of forgetfulness (sajdah al-sahw). The author begins by stating that sajdah al-sahw is wajib (obligatory) in cases of increase (ziyadah) or decrease (nuqsan) in the prayer. The 'increase' refers to additional actions that are wajib or fard being repeated, and 'decrease' refers to missing a wajib. The note clarifies: it is for forgetting a wajib, increasing a wajib, or repeating a fard. It is not for leaving a sunnah (supererogatory act). If a fard (obligatory pillar) is missed entirely, the prayer becomes invalid and sajdah al-sahw cannot fix it. The primary proof is the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forgot a rak'ah in 'Asr, completed it, then performed sajdah al-sahw after the final salam. This establishes that sajdah al-sahw is after the salam. The passage then details the Hanafi method: after the initial tashahhud and salam to the right, one performs two prostrations, then recites tashahhud, darud, and dua, and then gives salam to both sides. This is based on the hadith where the Prophet did exactly that after the deficiency. The author also provides evidence for sajdah al-sahw due to increase: the hadith of Abdullah (ibn Mas'ud) where the Prophet prayed five rak'at, was reminded, and performed sajdah al-sahw. For decrease, the hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhaynah (cut off here) also serves as proof. The footnotes reproduce the hadiths in simplified Urdu for clarity.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for an unintentional deficiency, increase, or misordering in the prayer.
وجب (wajib): A religious obligation less than fard, established by a zanni dalil; leaving it intentionally is sinful but not as grave as leaving a fard.
زيادة (ziyadah): Increase in the prayer, such as adding an extra rak'ah or repeating a wajib action unintentionally.
نقصان (nuqsan): Decrease, such as forgetting a wajib element (e.g., tashahhud) or missing a rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is sajdah al-sahw wajib?
A) Whenever any part of the prayer is missed, including sunnah.
B) When a wajib is missed or increased, or a fard is inadvertently repeated.
C) Only when an extra rak'ah is prayed.
D) When the imam makes a mistake in recitation.

Key Takeaway
Sajdah al-sahw is wajib to compensate for unintentional increase or decrease in wajib or fard acts in prayer, performed after salam with two prostrations and subsequent tashahhud.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Sujud al-Sahw and Dispute on Timing
Ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Sujud al-Sahw, identify its proofs, and compare the Hanafi, Shafi'i, and Maliki positions on timing.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib, performed after salam in the Hanafi school; timing differs among madhhabs based on different hadith.

Sujud al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) is a key compensatory act in salah. This lesson presents the Hanafi ruling, including its obligation and precise procedure. We will then examine the inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether it occurs before or after the final salam, a difference that has practical implications for every Muslim's prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Read the first part: 'Sujud al-Sahw is wajib in increase and decrease, after salam he performs two sajdahs then tashahhud and salam.' Identify the hukm level and timing.
Note that the text emphasizes 'after salam' and distinguishes wajib omission from fard omission.
2
Identify the opposing views
Locate the paragraph beginning 'Imam Shafi'i … before salam' and the following Maliki view. Note the key difference: Shafi'i says before salam; Maliki distinguishes increase (after) vs decrease (before).
3
Analyze the Hanafi proofs
The text cites the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn (for decrease) and Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (for increase). Confirm that both show the Prophet ﷺ gave salam first, performed sajdahs, then gave salam again.
The hadith are sahih, but their interpretation is debated.
4
Examine the opponents' proofs
The Shafi'i proof is the hadith of Abu Dawud where the Prophet ﷺ performed sajdahs before salam. The Maliki view uses both types of hadith. Understand how each school prioritizes its evidence.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Reflect: how does the timing affect the prayer? A Hanafi must do Sujud al-Sahw after salam; a Shafi'i before. The Maliki changes based on the nature of the error. This difference is the thamarah al-khilaf.
This shows that ikhtilaf is not merely academic but affects actual worship.

كتاب الصلوة
باب سجود السهو
[۲۹۷](۱) سجود السهو واجب في الزيادة والنقصان بعد السلام يسجد سجدتين ثم تشهد ويسلم. ضروری نوٹ سجود السهو : کوئی واجب بھول جائے یا واجب کی زیادتی ہو جائے یا فرائض مکرر ادا ہو جائیں تو اس کو گویا کہ پورا کرنے کے لئے سجدہ سہو واجب ہے۔ سنت کے چھوڑنے سے سجدہ سہو نہیں ہے۔ فرض چھوٹ جائے تو نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عمران بن حصين ن قال سلم رسول الله الله الله في ثلاث ركعات من العصر ثم قام فدخل الحجرة فقام رجل بسيط اليدين فقال اقصرت الصلوة يا رسول الله فخرج مغضبا فصلى الركعة التى كان ترك ثم سلم ثم سجد سجدتی السهو ثم سلم (الف ) ( مسلم شریف، باب فصل من ترک الرکعتین اونحوهما فلیتم مابقی و یسجد سجدتین بعد التسلیم ،ص۲۱۴، نمبر ۱۲۹۴٫۵۷۴؎ بخاری شریف ، باب هل یا خذ الا ام از اشک بقول الناس ،ص ۹۹ نمبر ۷۱۴ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الامام نبض فی الرکعتین ناسیا بص ۸۳ نمبر ۳۶۴ را بو داؤد شریف، باب السهو فی السجدتین، ص۱۵۳، نمبر ۱۰۱۸ اس باب کی آخری حدیث ہے ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کوئی واجب بھول جائے تو سلام کرے پھر سجدہ سہو کرے پھر سلام پھیرے۔ [۲۹۷] (۱) سجدہ سہو واجب ہے۔ واجبات کے زیادہ کر دینے میں یا کم کر دینے میں ۔ سلام کے بعد دو سجدے کرے پھر تشہد پڑھے اور سلام کرے۔

نتشر نماز میں واجب کی کمی رہ جائے یا زیادتی ہو جائے یا خلاف ترتیب ہو جائے تو اس کو پورا کرنے کے لئے سجدہ سہو کرنے گا ۔ اور سلام پھیرے گا۔ حفیہ کے نزدیک تشہد پڑھ کر دائیں جانب ایک سلام کرے پھر دو سجدہ سہو کرے پھر دوبارہ تشہد پڑھے، درود پڑھے، دعا پڑھے اور دوبارہ دونوں جانب سلام کرے۔ (1) اوپر کی حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے کہ آپ نے کمی زیادتی میں سلام کیا ہے پھر سجدہ سہو کیا ہے اور پھر دوبارہ سلام کیا ہے۔ زیادہ ہونے پر سجدہ سہو کیا ہو اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله قال صلى النبي الله الظهر خمسا فقالوا ازيد في الصلوة؟ قال وما ذاك قالوا صليت خمسا قال فتى رجله وسجد سجدتین (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب ما جاء فی القبلة ومن مر الا عادة على من سی ص ۵۸ نمبر ۴۰۴ ر مسلم شریف ، باب من مصلی شما الانجوه ص ۲۱۲ نمبر ۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں پانچ رکعت پڑھنے پر آپ نے سجدہ سہو کیا ہے جو زیادہ کرنے پر سجدہ سہو ہوا۔ کمی پر سجدہ سہو کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عبد الله بن بحينة انه قال صلى لنا رسول الله الله ركعتين
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے عصر کی تین رکعت میں سلام کر لیا۔ پھر کھڑے ہو گئے اور کمرے میں داخل ہوئے۔ پھر ایک آدمی کھڑا ہوا جسکے ہاتھ لمبے تھے تو پوچھایا رسول اللہ کی کیا نماز میں کمی ہوگئی ؟ تو آپ گفصہ میں نکلے اور وہ رکعت پڑھائی جو چھوٹ گئی تھی پھر سلام کیا پھر سجدہ سہو کیا پھر سلام کیا (ب) آپ نے ظہر کی پانچ رکعت پڑھائی تو لوگوں نے کہا کیا نماز میں زیادتی ہوگئی؟ تو آپ نے فرمایا یہ کیا بات ہے؟ لوگوں نے کہا آپ نے پانچ رکعتیں پڑھی ہیں۔ راوی کہتے ہیں آپ نے پاؤں موڑا اور دو سجدے کئے۔
