yتشهد ويسلم (۲) ويلزمه سجود السهو اذا زاد فى صلوته فعلا من جنسها ليس
صلى الله
ثم قام فلم يجلس فقام الناس معه فلما قضى صلوته وانتظر نا التسليم كبر فسجد سجدتين وهو جالس قبل التسليم ثم سلم صلى الله عليه وسلم (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب من قام من بنشین ولم يتشهد ص ۱۵۵نمبر ۱۰۳۴ار ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء في الامام شخصض فی الرکعتین ناسیا، ص ۸۳، نمبر ۳۶۴ نسائی شریف ، باب ما يفعل من قام من اشتین ناسیا ولم يتشهد ص ۱۳۷ نمبر ۱۲۲۳) اس حدیث میں کمی ہونے پر سجدہ کیا، قعدہ اولی نہ کرنے اور تشہد نہ پڑھنے پر سجدہ کیا۔ یہ بھی پتہ چلا کہ قعدہ اولے اور تشہد کا پڑھنا واجب ہے تو واجب کے چھوڑنے پر سجدہ سہو کیا۔ دو سلاموں کے درمیان دوبارہ تشہد پڑھے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عمران بن حصین ان النبي قال صلى بهم فسها فسجد سجدتين ثم تشهد ثم سلم (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب سجدتى السبو فيهما تشهد و تسلایم ص ۱۵۶ نمبر ۱۰۳۹ار ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی التشهد فی سجدتی السهوص ۹۰ نمبر ۳۹۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ دونوں سلاموں کے درمیان تشہد دوبارہ پڑھے گا۔ اور تشہد پڑھے گا تو اخیر میں درود شریف اور دعا بھی پڑھے۔ پہلا سلام نماز پوری ہونے کے لئے ہے اور دوسرا اسلام اس لئے ہے کہ سجدہ سہو نماز کے اندر ہو جائے تا کہ سجدہ سہو کے اندر کوئی کمی بیشی ہو جائے تو اس کو سجدہ کے ذریعہ پوری کی جاسکے۔ نانه امام شافعی کے نزدیک سلام سے پہلے سجدہ سہو کرے گا۔ ان کی دلیل او پر والی ابو داؤد کی حدیث ہے جس میں ہے۔ فسجد سجدتین وهو جالس قبل التسليم ثم سلم ( ابوداؤد شریف، باب من قام من میشین ولم یقت محمد ص ۱۵۵ نمبر ۱۰۳۴) اور امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ نماز میں کمی ہوئی ہو تو سلام سے پہلے سجدہ سہو کر یگا اور زیادتی ہوئی ہو تو سلام کے بعد سجدہ سہو کرے گا۔ انہوں نے دیکھا کہ سلام سے پہلے اور سلام کے بعد دونوں طرح سجدہ سہو ثابت ہے اس لئے انہوں نے یہ مسلک اختیار کیا۔
Book of Salah. Chapter of Sujud al-Sahw. [297](1) Sujud al-Sahw is obligatory in increase and decrease, after salam he performs two sajdahs then tashahhud and salam. Necessary note: Sujud al-Sahw: If any wajib is forgotten, or an addition of wajib occurs, or fard actions are repeated, then to complete it, Sujud al-Sahw is wajib. Sujud al-Sahw is not for leaving a sunnah. If a fard is missed, the salah becomes invalid. The evidence is this hadith: from Imran ibn Husayn: the Messenger of Allah ﷺ gave salam after three rak'ahs of Asr, then stood and entered his room. A man with long hands stood and said: 'Has the prayer been shortened, O Messenger of Allah?' He came out angry, prayed the rak'ah he had missed, then gave salam, then performed two sajdahs of forgetfulness, then gave salam. (Muslim, etc.) From this hadith it is understood: if one forgets a wajib, give salam, then perform Sujud al-Sahw, then give salam again. [297](1) Sujud al-Sahw is wajib; in increasing or decreasing wajibat, after salam perform two sajdahs, then recite tashahhud and salam. ... In the Hanafi school: recite tashahhud, give one salam to the right, then perform two sajdahs of forgetfulness, then recite tashahhud again, send salawat, make dua, and give salam to both sides again. (1) The above hadith proves that he ﷺ gave salam for increase or decrease, then did Sujud al-Sahw, then gave salam again. For increase, the evidence is: from Abdullah: the Prophet ﷺ prayed Zuhr five rak'ahs; they said: 'Has the prayer been increased?' He said: 'What is that?' They said: 'You prayed five.' He turned his leg and performed two sajdahs. (Bukhari, Muslim) ... For decrease, the evidence is: from Abdullah ibn Buhayna: he said: 'The Messenger of Allah ﷺ prayed two rak'ahs with us...' [then footnote and continuation]. [Page 210] ... Tashahhud and salam. (2) Sujud al-Sahw becomes incumbent upon him if he adds in his prayer an act of its kind that is not from it... [Then hadith of Abu Dawud about standing from two rak'ahs without sitting]. In this hadith, he performed sajdah for decrease, for not performing the first sitting and not reciting tashahhud. This also shows that the first sitting and reciting tashahhud are wajib, so he performed Sujud al-Sahw for leaving a wajib. The evidence for reciting tashahhud between the two salams: from Imran ibn Husayn: the Prophet ﷺ led them in prayer and forgot, then performed two sajdahs, then recited tashahhud, then gave salam (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). It is understood from this that he will recite tashahhud again between the two salams. And when he recites tashahhud, he will also recite salawat and dua at the end. The first salam is for completing the prayer, and the second salam is so that Sujud al-Sahw becomes part of the prayer, so that if any deficiency or excess occurs in it, it can be completed by the sajdah. According to Imam Shafi'i, Sujud al-Sahw will be before salam. Their evidence is the aforementioned hadith of Abu Dawud: 'He performed two sajdahs while sitting before salam, then gave salam.' Imam Malik says: If there is a decrease in the prayer, perform Sujud al-Sahw before salam; if there is an increase, perform it after salam. They saw that Sujud al-Sahw is proven both before and after salam, so they adopted this view.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samari presents the ruling on Sujud al-Sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) in the Hanafi school and then discusses the inter-madhhab dispute regarding its timing. The author first states the Hanafi ruling: Sujud al-Sahw is wajib (obligatory) for any increase or decrease in the prayer. The method is to give salam first, then perform two sajdahs, then recite tashahhud, and then give salam again. The author clarifies that this applies when a wajib (obligatory component) is forgotten or added, or when fard (essential) actions are repeated—but if a fard is missed entirely, the prayer becomes invalid. Sujud al-Sahw is not required for leaving a sunnah. The evidence is drawn from two sahih hadith: the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn (for decrease) and the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (for increase). The author then explains that in the Hanafi school, the complete procedure involves reciting tashahhud, giving one salam to the right, performing the two sajdahs, then reciting tashahhud again along with salawat and dua, and finally giving salam to both sides. This is based on a hadith from Imran ibn Husayn that mentions tashahhud between the two salams. Following this, the author presents the ikhtilaf (disagreement) of other Imams. Imam al-Shafi'i holds that Sujud al-Sahw should be performed before salam, citing the hadith of Abu Dawud where the Prophet ﷺ performed sajdahs before salam. Imam Malik distinguishes between cases: if the prayer has a decrease (e.g., forgetting a rak'ah), Sujud al-Sahw comes before salam; if an increase (e.g., extra rak'ah), it comes after salam. The Hanafi position is that Sujud al-Sahw must come after salam, as shown in the hadith of Imran ibn Husayn where the Prophet ﷺ gave salam, then did sajdahs, then gave salam again. The dispute arises from different hadith evidence and interpretations of their applicability. The text does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi (relied upon), but by presenting the Hanafi view first and in detail, it indicates that is the preferred position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for an omission or addition in salah.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory component whose omission requires Sujud al-Sahw.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in salah, including the shahada.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the correct sequence for Sujud al-Sahw after forgetting a wajib?
A) Perform two sajdahs before the final salam, then give salam.
B) Give salam, then perform two sajdahs, then recite tashahhud, then give salam again.
C) Give salam, then perform two sajdahs, then give salam again without tashahhud.
D) Perform two sajdahs, then give salam, then repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Sahw is a wajib compensatory act performed after the final salam in the Hanafi school, but its timing is disputed among madhhabs; understanding the proof and procedure is essential for correct salah.

What Necessitates Sujud al-Sahw: Adding an Act or Leaving a Wajib
Ruling on when Sujud al-Sahw is required due to addition or omission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two triggers of Sujud al-Sahw according to the Hanafi school and apply them to determine whether a given mistake requires Sujud al-Sahw.

Core Idea
Sujud al-Sahw becomes wajib when you add an act of the same kind as salah or leave a wajib; mere sunnah omissions do not require it.

This lesson explains the two specific conditions that trigger Sujud al-Sahw (prostration for forgetfulness) in the Hanafi school. You will learn to distinguish between additions that are 'of the same kind' and those that are not, and between wajib and sunnah omissions. The ruling is supported by a hadith from Sahih Muslim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two triggers
Read the passage and note that Sujud al-Sahw is required in two cases: (1) adding an act that is of the same kind as salah but not part of it, and (2) leaving a 'masnun' act—which the author clarifies means a wajib act established by the Sunnah.
2
Define 'act of the same kind' (fi'l min jinsiha)
The passage gives examples: performing two ruku' in one rak'ah or three sajdahs. These are actions that resemble the prescribed acts of salah (ruku', sajdah) but are extra and not part of the prayer's prescribed structure.
The act must be from the category of physical movements that constitute salah (like bowing, prostrating, standing, sitting).
3
Understand 'masnun' in context
The author explains that 'masnun' here refers to a wajib act, not a mustahab (recommended) sunnah. Leaving a mere sunnah (e.g., raising hands before ruku') does not require Sujud al-Sahw; only leaving a wajib (e.g., first sitting, tashahhud) triggers it.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school's terminology in this context.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
The hadith from Ibn Mas'ud (Allah be pleased with him) contains the general command: 'When a person increases or decreases, let him perform two sajdahs.' The Hanafi school interprets 'increase' as adding an act of the same kind, and 'decrease' as leaving a wajib.
The imperative 'falyasjud' indicates obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۹۸] (۲) مصلی کو سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا اگر زیادہ کر دے نماز میں ایسا فعل جو نماز کی جنس سے ہو لیکن نماز میں سے نہ ہو یا کوئی فعل مسنون چھوڑ دے اتنا مثلا رکوع یا سجدہ نماز کے فعل میں سے ہیں لیکن ایک ہی رکعت میں دو مرتبہ رکوع کر دے یا تین مرتبہ سجدہ کر دے تو دوسری مرتبہ کا رکوع یا تیر اسجدہ نماز میں سے نہیں ہے اگر چہ نماز کی جنس سے ہیں۔ اس لئے سجدۂ سہو لا زم ہوگا۔ اور فعل مسنون سے مراد فعل واجب ہے جو سنت نبوی سے ثابت ہے۔ کیونکہ سنت کو چھوڑ دیا تو نماز پوری ہو جائے گی اس کے لئے سجدہ سہو کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله قال صلينا مع رسول الله الا الله فاما زاد او نقص قال ابراهيم وايم الله ما جاء ذاک الا من قبلى قال قلنا يا رسول الله الا الله ماحدث في الصلوة شيء؟ فقال لا قال فقلنا له الذي صنع فقال اذا زاد الرجل او نقص فليسجد سجدتين قال ثم سجد سجدتين (ج) (مسلم شریف، باب من ترک الرکعتین اونحوها فلیتم مابقی و یسجد سجدتین بعد
[298] (2) Sujud al-Sahw becomes necessary for the one praying if he adds in his prayer an act that is of its kind but not part of it, or if he leaves a masnun act such that... for example, ruku' or sajdah are from the acts of prayer, but if he performs two ruku' in one rak'ah or three sajdahs, the second ruku' or third sajdah is not part of the prayer, although they are of its kind. Therefore Sujud al-Sahw becomes necessary. And by 'masnun act' is meant a wajib act that is established by the prophetic sunnah. Because if one leaves a sunnah, the prayer is still complete; there is no need for Sujud al-Sahw. There is a hadith: from Abdullah [ibn Mas'ud] who said: 'We prayed with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ... then he either increased or decreased.' Ibrahim said: 'By Allah, that only came from me.' He said: 'We said: O Messenger of Allah, has something new occurred in the prayer?' He said: 'No.' He said: 'We told him about what he had done.' He said: 'When a person increases or decreases, let him perform two sajdahs.' He said: 'Then he performed two sajdahs.' (Muslim, chapter: Whoever leaves two rak'ahs or similar, he should complete what remains and perform two sajdahs after...')
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage deals with the triggers (asbab) of Sujud al-Sahw according to the Hanafi school. The author states that Sujud al-Sahw becomes obligatory (wajib) if two conditions occur: (1) The worshipper adds an act that is 'of the same kind' as the acts of salah (min jinsiha) but not actually part of the prayer itself (laysa minha). For example, ruku' and sajdah are acts of the prayer, but if one performs two ruku' in one rak'ah or three sajdahs, the extra ruku' or sajdah is not part of the prescribed prayer even though it resembles it. Such an addition necessitates Sujud al-Sahw. (2) The worshipper leaves a 'masnun act' — but the author clarifies that here 'masnun' means a wajib (obligatory) act established by the Sunnah, not a mere sunnah. If a sunnah (non-obligatory recommended act) is left, the prayer remains valid and no Sujud is needed. Only leaving a wajib (like the first sitting or tashahhud) requires Sujud al-Sahw. The evidence is the hadith of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) which is general: 'When a person increases or decreases, let him perform two sajdahs.' This hadith is quoted from Sahih Muslim. The hadith is general and covers both increase and decrease, and the Hanafi school applies it specifically to additions of the same kind and omissions of wajib acts.

Key Terms
فعل من جنسها (fi'l min jinsiha): An act that is of the same category as the acts of salah (e.g., ruku', sajdah, standing) but not prescribed in that specific context.
فعل مسنون (fi'l masnun): In this context, a wajib act established by the Sunnah (like the first sitting and tashahhud).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following would require Sujud al-Sahw according to this passage?
A) Forgetting to recite a surah after al-Fatiha
B) Performing an extra ruku' in the same rak'ah
C) Forgetting to raise hands before ruku'
D) Reciting the tashahhud in the first sitting

Key Takeaway
Sujud al-Sahw is wajib only for adding an act of the same kind as salah or omitting a wajib; omitting a sunnah does not trigger it.

Sajdat al-Sahw: When It Is Required and the Evidence
General ruling with proof on sajdat al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when sajdat al-sahw is wajib, explain the prophetic evidence, and distinguish the Hanafi position from other schools.

Core Idea
Adding a like-action or omitting a wajib requires sajdat al-sahw; the Sunnah clarifies what is wajib.

This passage establishes the general principle that sajdat al-sahw compensates for an increase or omission in prayer. You will learn the two triggers for sajdat al-sahw and see how the Prophet’s own practice provides the proof. The commentary also highlights a key distinction: not every omitted sunnah requires this prostration—only those that are actually wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two triggers
Read the ruling: sajdat al-sahw is required when you add an action of the same genre (like a second bowing) or when you leave a ‘sunnah’ act—which the commentator explains means a wajib act.
The term ‘sunnah’ here is used in a technical sense for an obligation proven by the Sunnah.
2
Examine the prophetic evidence
Look at the hadith where the Prophet stood up without sitting (omitting the first sitting) and later prostrated before taslim. This shows that leaving a wajib act requires compensation.
The hadith is from Abu Daud and is ahad, giving zanni certainty.
3
Distinguish increase from omission
The passage defines increase as a like-action not originally in prayer (e.g., a third prostration) and omission as leaving a wajib (e.g., first sitting). Both require sajdat al-sahw.
A recommended act (sunnah) left out does not require it.
4
Compare the inter-madhhab dispute
The Shafi‘i school holds that sajdat al-sahw is performed before taslim in all cases, while the Maliki school differentiates based on deficiency or increase. The Hanafi position is based on the same hadith but interprets the timing differently.
The commentary mentions reciting tashahhud between two salams, highlighting the Hanafi view that sajdat al-sahw is part of the prayer.

حاشیہ : (الف) فرمایا آپ نے ہمیں دورکعت نماز پڑھائی پھر کھڑے ہوئے اور نہیں بیٹھے تو لوگ بھی آپ کے ساتھ کھڑے ہو گئے ۔ پس جب آپ نے نماز پوری کی اور ہم نے سلام کا انتظار کیا تو آپ نے تعمیر کہی اور دو سجدے کئے اس حال میں کہ آپ بیٹھے ہوئے تھیسلام سے پہلے ۔ پھر آپ نے سلام پھیرا (ب) آپ نے لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائی پس آپ بھول گئے پس آپ نے دو سجدے کئے پھر تشھد پڑھی پھر سلام کیا (ج) آپ نے فرمایا نماز میں زیادتی ہو جائے یا کمی ہو جائے ،ابراہیم راوی نے کہا کہ خدا کی قسم یہ وہم میری جانب سے ہے، راوی نے فرمایا ہم نے کہا یارسول اللہ نماز میں کوئی تبدیلی ہوگئی ہے؟ آپ نے فرمایا نہیں (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
The Sharh al-Thamiri, Vol. 1, p. 205, Book of Prayer. 'He recites tashahhud and makes taslim (2). Sajdat al-sahw is required if he increases in his prayer an action of its type that is not part of it...' Hadith: 'He stood up and did not sit...' Commentary: This hadith shows prostration for omission of first sitting and tashahhud, proving they are wajib. Evidence for reciting tashahhud between two salams is hadith of 'Imran. Dispute: Shafi'i says before taslim; Malik says before for deficiency, after for increase. [298] (2) Sajdat al-sahw is obligated if one adds a like-action (e.g., second bowing) or leaves a sunnah (by which is meant wajib). Hadith of 'Abdullah: 'If one increases or decreases, let him prostrate two prostrations.' Footnotes provide Urdu translations of hadith.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage opens with a general ruling that sajdat al-sahw is wajib when one adds an action of the same genre (min jinsiha) that is not from the prayer, or omits a sunnah (meaning wajib) act. The commentator then provides the proof from the hadith of the Prophet who stood up from the second rak'ah without sitting, and performed sajdat al-sahw before taslim. This establishes that the first sitting (qa'dah ula) and tashahhud are wajib. The passage also explains the procedure of reciting tashahhud again between the two salams after sajdat al-sahw, supported by the hadith of 'Imran ibn Husayn. Then an inter-madhhab dispute is presented: Imam Shafi'i holds that sajdat al-sahw should be before taslim based on the same hadith, while Imam Malik distinguishes between deficiency (before taslim) and increase (after taslim). The second part of the passage elaborates on the definition of 'increase of a like-action' and 'omission of sunnah' (wajib), with the hadith of 'Abdullah about the Prophet performing sajdat al-sahw for increase or decrease. The commentary clarifies that 'sunnah' here means a wajib act proven by the Sunnah, not a mere recommended act.

Key Terms
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness performed to compensate for an omission or addition in prayer.
فعل من جنسها (fi'l min jinsiha): An action that belongs to the same category as prayer acts (e.g., bowing, prostration) but is not part of the prescribed prayer sequence.
فعل مسنون (fi'l masnun): In this context, it means a wajib (obligatory) act established by the Sunnah, not a mere recommended act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, which of the following requires sajdat al-sahw?
A) Performing an extra prostration in a rak'ah
B) Reciting a different surah than intended
C) Delaying the prayer from its early time
D) Folding the hands below the navel

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-sahw is wajib in the Hanafi school for adding a like-action or omitting a wajib, as proven by the Prophet's practice.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Specific Causes for Sajdat al-Sahw: The Five Wajib Acts
Lists specific wajib omissions requiring sajdat al-sahw and the imam's role

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five specific wajib acts whose omission necessitates sajdat al-sahw and apply the ruling to a scenario where the imam recites loudly in a silent prayer.

Core Idea
Sajdat al-sahw is wajib for omitting any of five specified wajib acts: Fatiha, qunut, tashahhud, takbirat al-'idayn, and proper jahr/ikhfat.

This passage from Sharh al-Thamiri enumerates the precise wajib elements whose accidental omission must be compensated by sajdat al-sahw. Understanding these triggers is essential for any muṣallī to know when the prayer requires this corrective prostration.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five specific acts
List the five wajib acts mentioned: recitation of Surah al-Fatiha, qunut, tashahhud, takbirat al-'idayn, and correct jahr/ikhfat by the imam.
The first four are omissions of specific wajib components; the fifth is an error in modulation.
2
Understand what constitutes omission for each
For tashahhud, 'leaving' means either not sitting for its duration or not reciting it, as both are wajib. For jahr/ikhfat, reciting loudly where silence is required or vice versa is considered an omission of a wajib act.
The commentator explicitly clarifies the tashahhud case.
3
Examine the evidence
The primary evidence is the general hadith from Muslim: 'If one of you forgets, let him prostrate two prostrations.' For jahr/ikhfat, the athar from al-Thawri is cited, which directly mentions changing jahr/ikhfat as a cause for sajdat al-sahw.
The imperatives in the proofs indicate obligation (wujub) according to Hanafi usul.
4
Note the disagreement and Hanafi position
Some imams hold that changing jahr/ikhfat does not require sajdat al-sahw, citing the Prophet's occasional audible recitation in silent prayers. However, the Hanafi position, supported by the athar, is that sajdat al-sahw is wajib.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi view is the relied-upon position in the school.

كتاب الصلوة
منها او ترک قراءة فاتحة الكتاب او القنوت او التشهد او تكبيرات العيدين او جهر الامام فيما يخافت او خافت فيما يجهر [٣٠٠](۴) وسهو الامام يوجب على الـمـؤتـم السجود فان لم يسجد الامام لم يسجد المؤتم التسلیم ص ۲۱۳ نمبر۱۲۸۷٫۵۷۲ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من قال تیم علی اکثر نه ص۱۵۴ نمبر ۱۰۲۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں زیادتی ہو جائے یا کچھ واجب چھوٹ جائے تو سجدہ سہو کرے۔ (۲۹۹) (۳) یا سورۃ فاتحہ کی قرآت چھوڑ دی، یا دعائے قنوت چھوڑ دی یا تشہد چھوڑ دی، یا تکبیرات عیدین چھوڑ دی، یا امام نے قرآت جہری کر دی جس میں سری کرنا چاہئے ، یا سری کر دی جس میں جہری کرنا چاہئے۔
الشرح تشہد چھوڑ دی کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنا چھوڑ دیا، یا تشہد پڑھنا چھوڑ دیا تو چونکہ دونوں واجب ہیں اس لئے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبر میں ابوداؤد شریف کی حدیث ( نمبر ۱۰۳۴) گزرگئی ہے قام فلم يجلس، کہ آپ دورکعت کے بعد کھڑے ہو گئے اور قعدہ اولی میں نہیں بیٹھے تو سجدہ سہو کیا۔ اسی پر باقی واجبات کو قیاس کر لیں۔ کوئی واجب بھول جائے تو اس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ قال صلی بنا علقمة الظهر خمسا ... فاذا نسى احدكم فليسجد سجدتين (الف)(مسلم شریف، باب من صلی خمسا او نحوہ الخ ص ۲۱۳ نمبر ۱۲۸۵٫۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اگر بھول جاؤ تو سجدہ کرو۔ جہری قرات میں سری کردی اور سری قرآت میں جہری کر دی تو سجدہ سہو لازم ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عبد الرزاق عن الثوري قال اذا قمت فيما يجلس فيه او جلست فيما يقام فيه او جهرت فيما يخافت فيه او خافت فيما يجهر فيه ناسيا سجدت سجدتي السهو (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب اذا قام فیما یقعد فيه او قعد فيما يقام اوسلم فی شنی ج ثانی ص ۳۱۳ ، ابواب السہو نمبر ۳۴۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہری نماز میں سری قرآت کر دی اور سری نماز میں جہری قرآت کی تو سجدہ سہو کرے گا۔ نا کہ بعض ائمہ کے نزدیک سری کو جہری اور جہری کو سری کرنے سے سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ ان کا استدلال اس حدیث سے ہے عن قتادة كان النبى الله يقرأ في الركعتين من الظهر والعصر بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة وسورة يسمعنا الآية احيانا (بخاری شریف، باب القراءة في العصر ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۷۶۲ )
(۳۰۰) (۴) امام کے سہو سے مقتدی پر سجدہ واجب ہوگا ۔ پس اگر امام سجدہ نہ کرے تو مقتدی بھی سجدہ نہ کرے۔ امام ضامن ہے اس لئے امام پر سجدہ سہو لازم ہوا اور اس نے سجدہ سہو کیا تو چاہے مقتدی پر سجدہ سہو لازم نہ ہوا ہو پھر بھی مقتدی پر سجدہ لازم حاشیہ : ( پچھلے صفحہ سے آگے ) ہم نے آپ سے وہ بات کہی جو آپ نے کی تھی۔ آپ نے فرمایا اگر آدمی زیادہ کر دے یا کمی کر دے تو دو سجدے کرنا چاہئے ۔ راوی فرماتے ہیں کہ پھر آپ نے دوسجدہ سہو گئے (الف) آپ نے فرمایا تم میں سے کوئی بھول جائے تو دوسجدہ سہو کرنا چاہنے (ب) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا اگر جہاں بیٹھنا ہو وہاں کھڑا ہو جائے یا تم بیٹھ گئے جس میں کھڑا ہونا تھا یا جہری قرآت کر دی جس میں سری قرآت کرنی تھی یا سری در کت کر دی جس میں جہری قرآت کرنی تھی بھول کر دو سجدہ سہو کرے گا۔
From the Sharh al-Thamiri, Vol. 1, p. 206, Book of Prayer. 'From them: or leaving the recitation of Surah al-Fatiha, or qunut, or tashahhud, or the takbirs of the two 'Eids, or the imam reciting loudly where he should recite softly, or softly where he should recite loudly. [300] (4) And the imam's forgetfulness obligates the ma'mum to prostrate; if the imam does not prostrate, the ma'mum does not prostrate.' Commentary: This hadith shows that if one increases or leaves a wajib, he should perform sajdat al-sahw. (299) (3) Or leaving recitation of Fatiha, etc. Commentary: Meaning of leaving tashahhud is leaving the sitting to the extent of tashahhud or leaving the recitation of tashahhud. Since both are wajib, sajdat al-sahw is wajib. Evidence from the hadith of Abu Daud. Similarly, other wajibat are analogized. Evidence for forgetting a wajib is the hadith of 'Alqamah: 'If one of you forgets, let him prostrate two prostrations.' (Muslim). For jahr/ikhfat, the evidence is the athar from al-Thawri. Some imams hold that sajdat al-sahw is not required for changing jahr/ikhfat, citing the hadith that the Prophet would sometimes make audible a verse. (300) (4) The imam's forgetfulness makes sajdat al-sahw wajib on the ma'mum. If the imam does not prostrate, the ma'mum does not. The imam is the guarantor, so when sajdat al-sahw becomes wajib on him and he performs it, it becomes necessary on the ma'mum as well. Footnote: ...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage enumerates specific wajib acts whose omission necessitates sajdat al-sahw: recitation of Surah al-Fatiha, qunut, tashahhud, takbirat al-'idayn, and the imam's jahr/ikhfat in the wrong place. The commentator explains that 'leaving tashahhud' means either not sitting for its duration or not reciting it. The evidence is the hadith of the Prophet leaving the first sitting. For jahr/ikhfat, the evidence is the athar of al-Thawri, and a disagreement is noted: some imams do not require sajdat al-sahw for this, citing the Prophet's practice of occasionally making audible recitation. However, the Hanafi position is that it is wajib. The passage also covers the ruling that the imam's forgetfulness obligates sajdat al-sahw on the ma'mum, but if the imam does not perform it, the ma'mum does not, because the imam is the guarantor (al-imam damin).

Key Terms
فاتحة الكتاب (Fatiha al-Kitab): The opening chapter of the Quran, recited in every rak'ah of prayer.
قنوت (qunut): A supplication recited in the Witr prayer (or in Fajr according to some) during the standing.
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited while sitting in prayer.
تكبيرات العيدين (takbirat al-'idayn): The extra takbirs in the 'Eid prayers.
جهر (jahr): Audible recitation in prayer.
إخفات (ikhfat): Silent recitation in prayer.
سهو الإمام (sahw al-imam): Forgetfulness of the imam during prayer.
مأتم (ma'mum): The person praying behind an imam.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Sajdat al-sahw is wajib for forgetfully omitting any of the five specified wajib acts: Fatiha, qunut, tashahhud, takbirat al-'idayn, and correct jahr/ikhfat.

Ruling on Imam's Forgetfulness: The Ma'mum's Obligation
Rules on imam's forgetfulness affecting ma'mum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that the ma'mum must follow the imam in sajdat al-sahw only if the imam performs it, and identify the principle of 'al-imam damin'.

Core Idea
The ma'mum does not independently perform sajdat al-sahw; he follows the imam because the imam is the guarantor.

This brief but critical rule clarifies the relationship between the imam and ma'mum regarding sajdat al-sahw. The imam's forgetfulness triggers an obligation on the ma'mum, but only if the imam acts on it. This is based on the well-known Hanafi principle that the imam is the guarantor (damin) of the prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
The imam's forgetfulness obligates the ma'mum to perform sajdat al-sahw. However, if the imam does not perform sajdat al-sahw, the ma'mum should not perform it either.
The obligation on the ma'mum is contingent on the imam's action.
2
Understand the principle 'al-imam damin'
The imam is the guarantor (damin) meaning he carries responsibility for the prayer's validity. His sajdat al-sahw suffices for all followers.
This principle is a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh in congregational prayer.
3
Apply to a scenario
If the imam forgetfully omits a wajib and performs sajdat al-sahw, the ma'mum must follow him in the prostrations. If the imam forgets but does not realize and ends without sajdat al-sahw, the ma'mum should not perform it on his own, as the imam is responsible.
The ma'mum's individual sajdat al-sahw would be out of place because the obligation was shared.

The imam is the guarantor, so when sajdat al-sahw becomes wajib on him and he performs it, it becomes necessary on the ma'mum as well. Footnote: ...

Commentary
This passage enumerates specific wajib acts whose omission necessitates sajdat al-sahw: recitation of Surah al-Fatiha, qunut, tashahhud, takbirat al-'idayn, and the imam's jahr/ikhfat in the wrong place. The commentator explains that 'leaving tashahhud' means either not sitting for its duration or not reciting it. The evidence is the hadith of the Prophet leaving the first sitting. For jahr/ikhfat, the evidence is the athar of al-Thawri, and a disagreement is noted: some imams do not require sajdat al-sahw for this, citing the Prophet's practice of occasionally making audible recitation. However, the Hanafi position is that it is wajib. The passage also covers the ruling that the imam's forgetfulness obligates sajdat al-sahw on the ma'mum, but if the imam does not perform it, the ma'mum does not, because the imam is the guarantor (al-imam damin).

Key Terms
سهو الإمام (sahw al-imam): Forgetfulness of the imam during prayer.
مأتم (ma'mum): The person praying behind an imam.
ضامن (damin): Guarantor; the imam is responsible for the prayer's validity and covers the ma'mum's mistakes.

Key Takeaway
The ma'mum does not independently perform sajdat al-sahw; he follows the imam because the imam is the guarantor (damin).

Acts Requiring Sajdah al-Sahw
Enumeration of wajib omissions causing sajdah al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wajib acts whose omission necessitates sajdah al-sahw and cite the Hanafi evidence for each.

Core Idea
Forgetting a wajib act in prayer requires sajdah al-sahw — omission of a fard act invalidates the prayer.

In this passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamari, the author identifies specific wajib acts that, if forgotten during prayer, must be compensated with sajdah al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness). Understanding which omissions trigger this requirement is essential for maintaining the validity of one's salah. The passage also provides the textual evidence from hadith and athar that the Hanafi school relies upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
Recognize that sajdah al-sahw is a wajib act that compensates for forgetful omission of another wajib act in prayer.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because it is established by ahad hadith.
2
List the specific omissions that trigger sajdah
From the text, note the enumerated acts: leaving recitation of Fatihah, Qunut, Tashahhud, Takbirs of 'Eidain, or changing the mode of recitation (loud/quiet).
Also includes leaving a sunnah act? The text mentions 'sunnah' but the examples are all wajib. Clarify this with the commentary.
3
Locate the dalil for each case
The author cites hadith from Abu Dawud, Muslim, and athar from 'Abd al-Razzaq. Identify which proof corresponds to which omission.
General hadith about forgetfulness covers all cases; specific hadith about tashahhud and another about recitation mode.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyasjud' (let him prostrate) indicates obligation according to the Hanafi usul principle that al-amr yufid al-wujub.
Also, the Prophet's action of performing sajdah after standing up from the second rak'ah is evidence.
5
Note the ikhtilaf on loud/quiet recitation
Some imams (e.g., Shafi'i) do not require sajdah for this change, citing the Prophet allowing an ayah to be heard in silent prayers. The Hanafi response is that this does not negate the general rule.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

الشرح الثميرى الجزء الأوّل ۲۰۶ كتاب الصلوة منها او ترک فعلا مسنونا [۲۹۹](۳) او ترك قراءة فاتحة الكتاب او القنوت او التشهد او تكبيرات العيدين او جهر الامام فيما يخافت او خافت فيما يجهر التسلیم ص ۲۱۳ نمبر۱۲۸۷٫۵۷۲ ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من قال تیم علی اکثر نه ص۱۵۴ نمبر ۱۰۲۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز میں زیادتی ہو جائے یا کچھ واجب چھوٹ جائے تو سجدہ سہو کرے۔ (۲۹۹) (۳) یا سورۃ فاتحہ کی قرآت چھوڑ دی، یا دعائے قنوت چھوڑ دی یا تشہد چھوڑ دی، یا تکبیرات عیدین چھوڑ دی، یا امام نے قرآت جہری کر دی جس میں سری کرنا چاہئے ، یا سری کر دی جس میں جہری کرنا چاہئے۔ الشرح تشہد چھوڑ دی کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ تشہد کی مقدار بیٹھنا چھوڑ دیا، یا تشہد پڑھنا چھوڑ دیا تو چونکہ دونوں واجب ہیں اس لئے سجدہ سہو واجب ہوگا۔ اس کی دلیل مسئلہ نمبر میں ابوداؤد شریف کی حدیث ( نمبر ۱۰۳۴) گزرگئی ہے قام فلم يجلس، کہ آپ دورکعت کے بعد کھڑے ہو گئے اور قعدہ اولی میں نہیں بیٹھے تو سجدہ سہو کیا۔ اسی پر باقی واجبات کو قیاس کر لیں۔ کوئی واجب بھول جائے تو اس پر سجدہ سہو واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ قال صلی بنا علقمة الظهر خمسا ... فاذا نسى احدكم فليسجد سجدتين (الف)(مسلم شریف، باب من صلی خمسا او نحوہ الخ ص ۲۱۳ نمبر ۱۲۸۵٫۵۷۲) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اگر بھول جاؤ تو سجدہ کرو۔ جہری قرات میں سری کردی اور سری قرآت میں جہری کر دی تو سجدہ سہو لازم ہے۔ اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عبد الرزاق عن الثوري قال اذا قمت فيما يجلس فيه او جلست فيما يقام فيه او جهرت فيما يخافت فيه او خافت فيما يجهر فيه ناسيا سجدت سجدتي السهو (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب اذا قام فیما یقعد فيه او قعد فيما يقام اوسلم فی شنی ج ثانی ص ۳۱۳ ، ابواب السہو نمبر ۳۴۹۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہری نماز میں سری قرآت کر دی اور سری نماز میں جہری قرآت کی تو سجدہ سہو کرے گا۔ نا کہ بعض ائمہ کے نزدیک سری کو جہری اور جہری کو سری کرنے سے سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ ان کا استدلال اس حدیث سے ہے عن قتادة كان النبى الله يقرأ في الركعتين من الظهر والعصر بفاتحة الكتاب وسورة وسورة يسمعنا الآية احيانا (بخاری شریف، باب القراءة في العصر ص ۱۰۵ نمبر ۷۶۲ )
From it: or leaving a sunnah act, or leaving recitation of Fatihah, or al-Qunut, or al-Tashahhud, or the takbirs of the two 'Eids, or the imam reciting loudly where he should recite quietly or quietly where he should recite loudly. This hadith indicates that if there is an addition in prayer or some wajib is left, one should perform sajdah al-sahw. (299)(3) Or left recitation of Surah Fatihah, or left Du'a Qunut, or left Tashahhud, or left Takbirs of 'Eidain, or the imam recited loudly where he should recite quietly, or recited quietly where he should recite loudly. Commentary: The meaning of 'left Tashahhud' is that he left sitting for the amount of Tashahhud, or left reciting Tashahhud. Since both are wajib, sajdah al-sahw becomes wajib. Its proof is the hadith of Abu Dawud (no. 1034) that passed in the issue: he stood up and did not sit, so he performed sajdah al-sahw. Similarly, for other wajibat, if one forgets, sajdah al-sahw is wajib. The proof is the hadith: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) led us in Zuhr with five rak'ahs... if one of you forgets, let him perform two prostrations.' (Muslim). And for reciting loudly where quiet is prescribed and vice versa, sajdah al-sahw is required. Its proof is the athar from 'Abd al-Razzaq from al-Thawri: 'If you stand where you should sit, or sit where you should stand, or recite loudly where you should recite quietly, or recite quietly where you should recite loudly, forgetfully, you should perform two prostrations of forgetfulness.' This proves that if one recites loudly in a quiet prayer or quietly in a loud prayer, he should perform sajdah al-sahw. Some imams hold that this does not necessitate sajdah al-sahw, and they argue with the hadith of Qatadah that the Prophet would recite Fatihah and a surah in the first two rak'ahs of Zuhr and 'Asr and would sometimes let them hear an ayah.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage from Al-Sharh al-Thamari discusses the acts that necessitate sajdah al-sahw when forgotten in prayer. The author lists several specific omissions: leaving a sunnah act (though careful: sunnah here may mean wajib? The text says 'sunna' but then gives examples like Fatihah recitation which is wajib), leaving recitation of Surah al-Fatihah, leaving the qunut (in witr), leaving the tashahhud, leaving the takbirs of the two 'Eid prayers, and the imam reciting aloud where he should recite quietly or quietly where he should recite aloud. The commentary explains that all these are wajib acts; forgetting any of them requires sajdah al-sahw. The author provides evidence: first, he mentions a general hadith about any addition or omission requiring sajdah, then he gives specific proofs for each case. For tashahhud, he cites the hadith of the Prophet standing up from the second rak'ah without sitting, and then performing sajdah. For general forgetfulness, he cites the hadith of the Prophet leading five rak'ahs and then prostrating. For the case of silent vs. loud recitation, he cites an athar from al-Thawri. He also notes that some imams disagree on the recitation issue, using the hadith that the Prophet sometimes let them hear an ayah in silent prayers. However, the Hanafi position is that sajdah al-sahw is wajib in such cases.

Key Terms
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.
واجب (wajib): An obligatory act that if omitted forgetfully requires sajdah al-sahw; if omitted intentionally, sin and potential invalidity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Forgetting to recite Surah al-Fatihah
C) Forgetting to raise the hands for takbir
D) Forgetting to recite the adhan

Key Takeaway
Only the forgetful omission of a wajib act in prayer necessitates sajdah al-sahw; intentional omission or omission of a fard act has different consequences.

Imam's Forgetfulness and the Follower's Obligation
Rulings on sajdah al-sahw for imam and follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a follower performs sajdah al-sahw and explain the concept of the imam as damin.

Core Idea
The imam is the guarantor of the prayer: his forgetfulness binds the follower, but the follower's forgetfulness does not require sajdah.

In congregational prayer, the relationship between the imam and follower regarding forgetfulness is governed by clear rules. This lesson explores two key rulings: the imam's error obligates the follower to perform sajdah al-sahw, while the follower's own error triggers no sajdah for either. We will examine the evidence from hadith and the underlying rationale of the imam as the guarantor (damin).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
First, picture a follower in prayer: does he ever need to perform sajdah al-sahw? According to Hanafi fiqh, the follower must perform sajdah al-sahw only when the imam commits an error that requires it. The follower's own forgetfulness does not obligate sajdah.
The key distinction is between the imam's error and the follower's error.
2
Locate the Dalil
The text cites a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawud and al-Daraqutni: 'There is no sajdah upon the one behind the imam due to forgetfulness. If the imam forgets, then upon him and upon those behind him is sajdah. If the one behind the imam forgets, there is no sajdah upon him, and the imam suffices for him.' This is the primary proof.
The hadith explicitly states the ruling.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The operative phrase 'and the imam suffices for him' indicates that the follower is not required to act independently for his own forgetfulness. The imam's prayer covers the follower's minor errors, hence no sajdah.
This leads to the concept of damin (guarantor).
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) allow the follower to perform sajdah al-sahw independently if the imam does not. The Hanafi school restricts it to following the imam.
The Hanafi position relies on the hadith and the principle of following the imam.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi as it is based on clear textual evidence and the principle of damin. The ruling is established in the zahir al-riwayah.
No significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists on this ruling.

(300)(4) The forgetfulness of the imam obligates the follower to perform sajdah. If the imam does not perform sajdah, the follower does not perform sajdah. ... (301)(5) If the follower forgets, the imam is not obligated to perform sajdah. ... (2) And whoever forgets the first sitting, then remembers while he is closer to sitting, he should return and sit and recite tashahhud; if he is closer to standing, he should not return and should perform two prostrations of forgetfulness. ...
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This section from Al-Sharh al-Thamari covers the relationship between the imam and follower regarding sajdah al-sahw. It states two key rulings: (1) If the imam forgets and commits an error that requires sajdah al-sahw, the follower must follow the imam in performing sajdah al-sahw. If the imam does not perform it, the follower should not perform it either, because the imam is the guarantor (damin) of the prayer. (2) If the follower forgets, the imam is not required to perform sajdah al-sahw, and the follower himself does not perform it either. The reasoning is that the follower is a follower (tabi'), and his forgetfulness does not affect the imam; if the follower performed sajdah on his own, he would be dissenting from the imam, which is not allowed. The evidence includes the hadith of the Prophet leading the prayer and forgetting the first sitting, and the hadith that the follower's forgetfulness does not require sajdah. The lesson emphasizes that the imam's forgetfulness binds the follower, but not vice versa.

Key Terms
مؤتم (mu'tamm): The person praying behind an imam (follower).
ضامن (damin): The imam is the guarantor of the prayer, meaning his forgetfulness includes the follower.
سجدہ سہو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, performed to compensate for errors in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an imam commits an error that requires sajdah al-sahw but does not perform it, what should the follower do according to the Hanafi school?
A) The follower performs sajdah al-sahw alone.
B) The follower does not perform sajdah al-sahw and continues the prayer.
C) The follower reminds the imam to perform sajdah.
D) The follower repeats the prayer after the imam finishes.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the imam's forgetfulness obligates the follower to perform sajdah al-sahw, but the follower's own forgetfulness does not require sajdah because the imam is the guarantor.

Forgetting the First Sitting — The Hanafi Rule
Ruling on forgetting the first sitting with hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for forgetting the first sitting and identify when to return versus when to perform sajdah al-sahw, using the hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhaynah as proof.

Core Idea
Forgetting the first sitting: return if closer to sitting; if closer to standing, continue and perform sajdah al-sahw.

This lesson explains the precise Hanafi ruling when a person forgets the first tashahhud in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs. The key distinction is how close the person is to completing the standing position. The ruling is derived from the action of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as narrated by Abdullah ibn Buhaynah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is forgetting the first sitting. The ruling: if closer to sitting, return; if closer to standing, do not return but perform sajdah al-sahw.
The first sitting is itself a wajib in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhaynah where the Prophet stood up and did not sit, then performed sajdah al-sahw.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of not returning to sitting after full standing indicates that returning is incorrect in that posture. His sajdah al-sahw compensates for the omission.
4
Note the condition
The condition is proximity: the person must be closer to sitting or closer to standing at the moment of remembering.
5
Observe the cross-madhhab difference
Compare with the Shafi'i view that the first sitting is sunnah and one may return only before standing fully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۰۲) (۲) ومن سهى عن القعدة الاولى ثم تذكر وهو الى حال القعود اقرب عاد فجلس وتشهد وان كان الى حال القيام ہو گا (۲) اس کی دلیل حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن لجينة انه قال صلى لنا رسول الله ركعتين ثم قام فلم يجلس فقام الناس معه فلما قضى صلوته وانتظرنا التسليم كبر فسجد سجدتين وهو جالس قبل التسليم ثم سلم صلى الله عليه وسلم (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من قام من شتین ولم يتشهد ص ۱۵۵ نمبر ۱۰۳۴ار ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الامام ينهض في الركعتين ناسیاص ۸۳ نمبر ۳۶۵ر مسلم شریف، باب اذ انسی الجلوس في الركعتين فليسجد سجدتین قبل اى يسلم ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۵۷۰ ) اس حدیث میں امام پر سجدہ سہو تھا تو مقتدیوں کو بھی اس کی اقتدا میں کرنا پڑا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام کی وجہ سے مقتدی پر بھی سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا ۔ [۳۰۱) (۵) پس اگر مقتدی بھول جائے تو امام کو سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا اور نہ مقتدی کو سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا ۔ (1) مقتدی تابع ہے اس لئے امام کے خلاف ہو کر سجدہ سہو نہیں کر سکتا اور نہ تابع کی وجہ اسے اصل پر لازم ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن عمر عن النبي الله قال ليس على من خلف الامام سهو فان سها الامام فعليه وعلى من - خلفه السهو وان سها من خلف الامام فـليــس عـليـه سهو والامام کافیه (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب ليس على المقتدی سہو وعلیہ سہوالامام ض اول ص ۳۶۵ نمبر ۱۳۹۸) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ مقتدی کے سہو سے امام پر سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا اور امام کے سہو سے مقتدی پر لازم ہوگا (۳) اس قسم کا اثر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب حل على من خلف الامام سہوج ثانی ص ۳۱۵ نمبر ۳۵۰۶) میں موجود ہے۔
(302)(2) And whoever forgets the first sitting, then remembers while he is closer to sitting, he should return and sit and recite tashahhud; if he is closer to standing, he should not return and should perform two prostrations of forgetfulness. (2) The evidence for this is the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Buhaynah: 'The Messenger of Allah led us in two rak'ahs, then stood up and did not sit, so the people stood with him. When he completed his prayer and we waited for the taslim, he said takbir and prostrated two prostrations while sitting before the taslim, then he gave taslim.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Muslim). This hadith shows that when the imam forgot, sajdah al-sahw was required for him and the followers followed him. ...
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This lesson, from Al-Sharh al-Thamari, deals with the specific case of forgetting the first sitting (qad'ah ula) in a prayer of more than two rak'ahs. The ruling distinguishes based on how far the person has moved towards standing. If, after forgetting to sit, the person remembers while he is still closer to sitting (i.e., has not yet fully stood up), he should return to the sitting position and recite the tashahhud. In this case, no sajdah al-sahw is required because the error was corrected immediately. However, if he has already fully stood up (closer to standing), he should not sit back down; instead, he continues the prayer and performs sajdah al-sahw at the end. The evidence is the famous hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhaynah, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forgot the first sitting and stood up, but then after completing the prayer, he performed sajdah al-sahw before the taslim. This hadith shows both the ruling (not sitting back after full standing) and the compensation (sajdah al-sahw).

Key Terms
قعدہ اولی (qa'dah ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in prayers of three or four rak'ahs.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostrations of forgetfulness performed to compensate for an omission or error in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone forgets the first sitting and stands up fully, what should he do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Return to sitting and then continue
B) Continue standing and perform sajdah al-sahw at the end
C) Repeat the prayer from the beginning
D) Perform sajdah al-sahw immediately

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on forgetting the first sitting hinges on proximity: return if close to sitting, otherwise perform sajdah al-sahw.

The Follower and Sajdah al-Sahw
Ruling on follower's sajdah al-sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when the follower (muqtadi) is required to perform sajdah al-sahw and when the imam's sajdah suffices, using the hadith of Umar.

Core Idea
The follower's forgetfulness does not require sajdah al-sahw; only the imam's forgetfulness triggers it for both.

This lesson covers the rules of sajdah al-sahw for the person praying behind an imam. The hadith and athar cited show that the follower is not burdened with sajdah al-sahw for his own forgetfulness; rather, he follows the imam in sajdah al-sahw if the imam forgets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the follower
The follower does not perform sajdah al-sahw for his own forgetfulness.
This is derived from the hadith: 'ليس على من خلف الامام سهو'.
2
Identify the ruling when the imam forgets
If the imam forgets and performs sajdah al-sahw, the follower must follow him in that.
The hadith says: 'فان سها الامام فعليه وعلى من خلفه السهو'.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) and the athar from Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq.
4
Analyze the dalil
The hadith explicitly negates sajdah for the follower's own forgetfulness and affirms it when the imam forgets.
5
Understand the principle
The follower is a follower (tabi'), so his error is covered by the imam; he cannot lead in error.

[۳۰۲) (۲) ومن سهى عن القعدة الاولى ثم تذكر وهو الى حال القعود اقرب عاد فجلس وتشهد وان كان الى حال القيام ہو گا (۲) اس کی دلیل حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن لجينة انه قال صلى لنا رسول الله ركعتين ثم قام فلم يجلس فقام الناس معه فلما قضى صلوته وانتظرنا التسليم كبر فسجد سجدتين وهو جالس قبل التسليم ثم سلم صلى الله عليه وسلم (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من قام من شتین ولم يتشهد ص ۱۵۵ نمبر ۱۰۳۴ار ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الامام ينهض في الركعتين ناسیاص ۸۳ نمبر ۳۶۵ر مسلم شریف، باب اذ انسی الجلوس في الركعتين فليسجد سجدتین قبل اى يسلم ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۵۷۰ ) اس حدیث میں امام پر سجدہ سہو تھا تو مقتدیوں کو بھی اس کی اقتدا میں کرنا پڑا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام کی وجہ سے مقتدی پر بھی سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا ۔ [۳۰۱) (۵) پس اگر مقتدی بھول جائے تو امام کو سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا اور نہ مقتدی کو سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا ۔ (1) مقتدی تابع ہے اس لئے امام کے خلاف ہو کر سجدہ سہو نہیں کر سکتا اور نہ تابع کی وجہ اسے اصل پر لازم ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن عمر عن النبي الله قال ليس على من خلف الامام سهو فان سها الامام فعليه وعلى من - خلفه السهو وان سها من خلف الامام فـليــس عـليـه سهو والامام کافیه (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب ليس على المقتدی سہو وعلیہ سہوالامام ض اول ص ۳۶۵ نمبر ۱۳۹۸) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ مقتدی کے سہو سے امام پر سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا اور امام کے سہو سے مقتدی پر لازم ہوگا (۳) اس قسم کا اثر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب حل على من خلف الامام سہوج ثانی ص ۳۱۵ نمبر ۳۵۰۶) میں موجود ہے۔
(302)(2) And whoever forgets the first sitting, then remembers while he is closer to sitting, he should return and sit and recite tashahhud; if he is closer to standing, he should not return and should perform two prostrations of forgetfulness. (2) The evidence for this is the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Buhaynah: 'The Messenger of Allah led us in two rak'ahs, then stood up and did not sit, so the people stood with him. When he completed his prayer and we waited for the taslim, he said takbir and prostrated two prostrations while sitting before the taslim, then he gave taslim.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Muslim). This hadith shows that when the imam forgot, sajdah al-sahw was required for him and the followers followed him. ...
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This lesson, from Al-Sharh al-Thamari, deals with the specific case of forgetting the first sitting (qad'ah ula) in a prayer of more than two rak'ahs. The ruling distinguishes based on how far the person has moved towards standing. If, after forgetting to sit, the person remembers while he is still closer to sitting (i.e., has not yet fully stood up), he should return to the sitting position and recite the tashahhud. In this case, no sajdah al-sahw is required because the error was corrected immediately. However, if he has already fully stood up (closer to standing), he should not sit back down; instead, he continues the prayer and performs sajdah al-sahw at the end. The evidence is the famous hadith of Abdullah ibn Buhaynah, where the Prophet (peace be upon him) forgot the first sitting and stood up, but then after completing the prayer, he performed sajdah al-sahw before the taslim. This hadith shows both the ruling (not sitting back after full standing) and the compensation (sajdah al-sahw).

Key Terms
قعدہ اولی (qa'dah ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in prayers of three or four rak'ahs.
مقتدی (muqtadi): The person praying behind the imam in congregational prayer.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostrations of forgetfulness performed to compensate for an omission or error in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when does a follower (muqtadi) need to perform sajdah al-sahw?
A) Whenever he forgets a wajib
B) Only when the imam performs sajdah al-sahw
C) Whenever he forgets any element of prayer
D) He never performs sajdah al-sahw

Key Takeaway
The follower does not perform sajdah al-sahw for his own forgetfulness; he follows the imam's sajdah if the imam forgets.

If the Follower Forgets in Prayer, the Imam is Not Obligated to Perform Sajda Sahw
Ruling with proof: follower's forgetfulness negates sajda sahw

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's forgetfulness and apply the hadith proof to identify when sajda sahw is required or not.

Core Idea
The follower's forgetfulness does not obligate sajda sahw on him or the imam — the imam suffices.

This passage addresses a common question in congregational prayer: what happens if the follower (mu'tam) forgets a wajib? The Hanafi school rules that the follower does not perform sajda sahw independently, nor does the imam perform it on his behalf. The proof is a hadith from the Prophet (ﷺ) that establishes the imam's prayer as sufficient.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the follower's forgetfulness in prayer. The ruling: no sajda sahw is required from either the imam or the follower.
This is a negation of obligation, not a positive obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith narrated from Umar, recorded by Dar Qutni, stating 'There is no sahu on the follower...'
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit phrase 'laysa ala man khalfa al-imam sahw' directly negates any sahu (forgetfulness) obligation on the follower.
The pronoun 'man' includes all types of forgetfulness.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) hold that the follower must perform sajda sahw for his own significant forgetfulness.
The difference stems from interpreting the hadith's scope and the follower's responsibility.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the clear negation in the hadith and the principle that the follower is subordinate (tabi') to the imam.
The follower's prayer is valid through the imam's sufficiency.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان سهى المؤتم لم يلزم الامام السجود
پس اگر مقتدی بھول جائے تو امام کو سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا اور نہ مقتدی کو سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا ۔ (1) مقتدی تابع ہے اس لئے امام کے خلاف ہو کر سجدہ سہو نہیں کر سکتا اور نہ تابع کی وجہ اسے اصل پر لازم ہوگا (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن عمر عن النبي الله قال ليس على من خلف الامام سهو فان سها الامام فعليه وعلى من خلفه السهو وان سها من خلف الامام فليس عليه سهو والامام كافيه (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب ليس على المقتدی سہو وعلیہ سہوالامام ض اول ص ۳۶۵ نمبر ۱۳۹۸) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ مقتدی کے سہو سے امام پر سجدہ سہو لازم نہیں ہوگا اور امام کے سہو سے مقتدی پر لازم ہوگا (۳) اس قسم کا اثر مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب حل على من خلف الامام سہوج ثانی ص ۳۱۵ نمبر ۳۵۰۶) میں موجود ہے۔
If the follower forgets, the imam is not obligated to perform sajda sahw. Then if the follower forgets, the imam will not be obligated to do sajda sahw, nor will the follower be obligated to do sajda sahw. (1) The follower is a follower, so he cannot perform sajda sahw contrary to the imam, and his forgetfulness does not obligate the imam. (2) There is a hadith from Umar from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'There is no sahu on the one who follows the imam; if the imam forgets, then sahu is upon him and those behind him; and if the one behind the imam forgets, then there is no sahu upon him, and the imam suffices.' This hadith proves that from the follower's forgetfulness, sajda sahw is not obligatory on the imam, and from the imam's forgetfulness, it is obligatory on the follower. (3) A similar athar is found in Musannaf Abdur Razzaq.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the relationship between the imam and follower (mu'tam) regarding forgetfulness (sahu) in prayer. The author states that if the follower forgets, the imam is not required to perform sajda sahw, nor is the follower himself required to do so. The reason given is that the follower is subordinate (tabi') to the imam; he cannot act independently by performing sajda sahw when the imam does not, nor does his forgetfulness burden the imam. The proof is a hadith from Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared that there is no sahu upon the follower; if the imam forgets, sahu is upon him and the followers, but if the follower forgets, there is no sahu upon him—the imam is sufficient. This establishes that the follower's forgetfulness is not a cause for sajda sahw, while the imam's forgetfulness obligates both. The author also cites an athar from Musannaf Abdur Razzaq supporting this position.

Key Terms
مؤتم (mu'tam): A person praying behind an imam; a follower in congregational prayer.
سهو (sahu): Forgetfulness during prayer that necessitates sajda sahw.
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Two prostrations performed to compensate for forgetfulness in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The imam must perform sajda sahw on his behalf.
B) The follower must perform sajda sahw independently.
C) Neither the imam nor the follower performs sajda sahw; the imam suffices.
D) The follower must repeat the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The follower's forgetfulness is covered by the imam; no sajda sahw is required.

Forgetting the First Sitting in Prayer
Provides the ruling and evidence for when one forgets the first sitting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on forgetting the first sitting by determining whether to return or perform sajda sahw based on the proximity to standing.

Core Idea
If you forget the first sitting, return only if not yet fully standing; otherwise, perform sajda sahw.

The first sitting (qada ula) is a wajib element in the Hanafi prayer. Forgetting it raises a common question: should you return to sit or continue? The Prophet's guidance, preserved in the hadith of Mughira bin Shu'ba and the action of the Prophet reported by Abdullah bin Lujaina, draws a clear line based on how far you have risen. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its proof, preparing you to handle this situation with confidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
In a prayer of three or four rak'ahs, the first sitting after the initial two rak'ahs is a wajib (obligatory but not fard). Forgetting it triggers a corrective action.
Hanafi: wajib, not fard; omission requires sajda sahw or return.
2
Locate the dalil
The source quotes the hadith of Mughira bin Shu'ba: 'When the imam stands after two rak'ahs, if he remembers before standing straight, let him sit; if he is fully standing, let him not sit and perform two prostrations of sahu.' Also the hadith of Ibn Lujaina shows the Prophet's action.
Hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for wajib rulings.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit condition 'before standing straight' vs. 'after standing straight' establishes that the decisive factor is the moment of remembrance. The Prophet's action confirms that if fully standing, returning would disrupt the prayer, so sajda sahw compensates.
The contrast is clear, making the ruling operational.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) consider the first sitting sunnah, not wajib, and may allow return after full standing or not require sajda sahw.
This difference affects the need for sajda sahw.
5
Apply to practice
If you remember while still bending (closer to sitting), return; if you have fully straightened (closer to standing), do not return and complete the prayer with two sajda sahw before taslim.
The Hanafi mufta bihi position: do not return if fully standing.

ومن سهى عن القعدة الاولى ثم تذكر وهو الى حال القعود اقرب عاد فجلس وتشهد وان كان الى حال القيام اقرب لم يعد ويسجد للسهو
اس کی دلیل حدیث میں ہے عن عبد الله بن لجينة انه قال صلى لنا رسول الله ركعتين ثم قام فلم يجلس فقام الناس معه فلما قضى صلوته وانتظرنا التسليم كبر فسجد سجدتين وهو جالس قبل التسليم ثم سلم صلى الله عليه وسلم (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من قام من شتین ولم يتشهد ص ۱۵۵ نمبر ۱۰۳۴ار ترمذی شریف ، باب ماجاء فی الامام ينهض في الركعتين ناسیاص ۸۳ نمبر ۳۶۵ر مسلم شریف، باب اذ انسی الجلوس في الركعتين فليسجد سجدتین قبل اى يسلم ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۵۷۰ ) اس حدیث میں امام پر سجدہ سہو تھا تو مقتدیوں کو بھی اس کی اقتدا میں کرنا پڑا۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امام کی وجہ سے مقتدی پر بھی سجدہ سہو لازم ہوگا ۔
[۳۰۲ (۶) جو قعدہ اولی بھول جائے پھر یاد آئے اس حال میں کہ بیٹھنے کے زیادہ قریب ہو تو لوٹ جائے اور بیٹھے اور تشہد پڑھے، اور اگر کھڑے ہونے کے زیادہ قریب ہو تو نہ ملے تے اور سجدہ سہو کرے۔ قعدہ اولی واجب ہے لیکن اس کو بھول کر کھڑا ہو گیا تو اور کھڑے ہونے کے قریب ہو گیا تب یاد آیا تو اب دوبارہ نہ بیٹھے بلکہ کھڑے ہو کر آگے والے اعمال کرے۔ کیونکہ اب بیٹھنے میں قیام کی تاخیر ہوگی۔ اور بیٹھنے کے قریب تھا کہ یاد آیا تو ابھی کھڑا نہیں ہوا ہے اس لئے بیٹھنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اور سجدہ سہو بھی لازم نہیں ہوگا۔
حدیث میں ہے عن مغيرة بن شعبة قال قال رسول الله الا الله اذا قام الامام في الركعتين فان ذكر قبل ان يستوى قائما فليجلس فان اسروى قائما فلا يجلس ويسجد سجدتي السهو (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب من نسی ان بتشهد وهو جالس ص ۲۵۵ نمبر ۱۰۳۶ار دار قطنی ، باب الرجوع الی القعود قبل استتمام القیام ج اول ص ۳۶۷ نمبر ۱۴۰۳)
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے ہمیں دو رکعت نماز پڑھائی پھر کھڑے ہوئے اور نہیں بیٹھے تو لوگ بھی آپ کے ساتھ کھڑے ہو گئے پس جب آپ نے نماز پوری کی اور ہم نے سلام پھیرنے کا انتظار کیا تو آپ نے تکبیر کہی اور دو سجدے کئے اس حال میں کہ بیٹھے ہوئے تھے سلام سے پہلے پھر سلام پھیرا (ب ) آپ نے فرمایا جو امام کے پیچھے ہو اس پر سجدہ سہو نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر امام بھول جائے تو اس پر سجدہ سہو ہے اور جو اس کے بچھی ہیں اس پر بھی سجدہ سہو ہے۔ اور اگر جو امام کی پیچھے ہے وہ بھول گیا تو اس پر سجدہ سہو نہیں ہے۔ امام اس کو کافی ہے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا جب امام دو رکعت پر کھڑا ہو جائے ، پس اگر مکمل کھڑا ہونے سے پہلے یاد آ جائے تو بیٹھ جانا چاہئے۔ پس اگر مکمل کھڑا ہو چکا ہو تو نہ بیٹھے اور دوسجدہ سہو کرے۔
And if one forgets the first sitting, then remembers while he is closer to the state of sitting, he returns and sits and recites the tashahhud; and if he is closer to the state of standing, he does not return and performs sajda sahw. Its evidence is a hadith from Abdullah bin Lujaina: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed two rak'ahs with us, then he stood up and did not sit, so the people stood with him. When he completed his prayer and we were waiting for the taslim, he said takbir and performed two prostrations while sitting before the taslim, then he said taslim.' (Reference: Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Muslim) This hadith shows that the imam required sajda sahw, so the followers had to follow him. Thus it is understood that the imam's forgetfulness obligates sajda sahw upon the follower.
[302] (6) Whoever forgets the first sitting, then remembers when he is closer to sitting, he should return, sit, and recite tashahhud. But if he is closer to standing, he should not return and should perform sajda sahw. The first sitting is wajib, but if he forgot and stood up, and when he was closer to standing he remembered, then he should not sit down but continue standing and complete the prayer, because sitting now would delay the standing. And if he was closer to sitting when he remembered, it is not objectionable to sit, and sajda sahw is not required. There is a hadith from Mughira bin Shu'ba: the Prophet said: 'When the imam stands up after two rak'ahs, if he remembers before standing straight, let him sit; if he is fully standing, let him not sit and perform two prostrations of sahu.' (Reference: Abu Dawud, Dar Qutni) Commentary: (a) He prayed two rak'ahs with us, then he stood and did not sit, so the people stood with him... (b) He said: 'There is no sahu on the one who follows the imam...' (c) He said: 'When the imam stands up after two rak'ahs, if he remembers before standing fully, he should sit; if he is fully standing, he should not sit and perform sajda sahw.'
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and evidence for when someone forgets the first sitting (qada ula) in prayer. The matn states: if the person is physically closer to sitting (i.e., has not fully risen), he should return, sit, and recite tashahhud; if he is closer to standing (i.e., has fully risen), he should not return and instead perform sajda sahw. The reason is that the first sitting is wajib (obligatory, but not fard), so forgetting it requires compensation via sajda sahw. However, if he is still near the sitting position, returning does not disrupt the prayer's order significantly. The author cites two hadiths: one from Abdullah bin Lujaina, where the Prophet himself stood up after two rak'ahs, forgot the first sitting, and later performed sajda sahw before taslim. This shows that the imam's forgetfulness necessitates sajda sahw for the followers as well. The second hadith from Mughira bin Shu'ba explicitly states the principle: if the imam (or any person) stands up after two rak'ahs, if he remembers before standing straight, he should sit; if he is fully upright, he should not sit and should perform two prostrations of sahu. The commentary clarifies that the first sitting is wajib, so forgetting it requires sajda sahw only if one has fully stood up; otherwise, returning is preferable. The footnote translates the three hadith references for clarity.

Key Terms
قعدة اولى (qada ula): The first sitting after two rak'ahs in a prayer of three or four rak'ahs.
تشهد (tashahhud): The recitation of 'At-tahiyyat...' during sitting in prayer.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Two extra prostrations performed at the end of prayer to compensate for forgetfulness or omission of a wajib element.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Continue standing and perform sajda sahw at the end.

D) Abort the prayer and start over.

Key Takeaway
The decisive moment for returning to the first sitting is the point of fully standing; before that, return; after that, continue and perform sajda sahw.

Forgetting the Final Sitting and Standing for a Fifth Rak'ah
Ruling on forgetting the final sitting and standing for a fifth rak'ah before prostration, with evidence and explanation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on forgetting the final sitting and standing for a fifth rak'ah, distinguishing between before and after prostration, and apply the principle that omitting a fard invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Forgetting the final sitting and adding a fifth rak'ah: return before prostration; after prostration, it becomes nafl and must be repeated.

In the Hanafi school, the final sitting (qada akhir) is considered a fard (pillar) of prayer. Forgetting it and mistakenly standing for a fifth rak'ah triggers a specific ruling depending on whether the prostration of the extra rak'ah has been performed. This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri explains the remedy: return if possible, otherwise salvage the prayer as nafl and repeat the fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is forgetting the final sitting and standing for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard prayer. The ruling has two branches: before prostration in the fifth, and after prostration.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? An athar from Hammad (a tabi'i) recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq: 'If a man prays five [rak'ahs] and does not sit in the fourth, then he should add a sixth, then say taslim, then start his prayer anew.'
This athar is used as evidence for the case where prostration in the fifth has occurred.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this athar prove the ruling? The athar directs adding a sixth rak'ah and repeating the fard, indicating that the original prayer becomes nafl (since five rak'ahs are odd, adding a sixth makes an even number of nafl). This supports the Hanafi position that the fard is invalidated and transformed into nafl.
The Hanafi school uses istihsan to avoid complete nullification of the prayer due to forgetfulness.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any other school disagree? Yes, Shafi'is consider the final sitting as sunnah, not fard, so their ruling would be different: the prayer would be valid with sajda sahw only, without needing to add a sixth or repeat.
This difference stems from the categorization of the final sitting.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon and why? The Hanafi position is mufta bihi in the school. The ruling is based on the principle that leaving a fard invalidates the prayer, but istihsan allows conversion to nafl, supported by the athar from Hammad.
The key distinction is based on whether prostration in the extra rak'ah has occurred, which 'strengthens' the extra rak'ah and prevents cancellation.

Source Text

(۳۰۳) (۷) اگر قعدہ اخیرہ بھول گیا اور پانچویں رکعت کی طرف کھڑا ہو گیا تو قعدہ اخیرہ کی طرف لوٹے گا جب تک سجدہ نہ کیا ہو اور پانچویں رکعت کولغو کرے اور سجدہ سہو کرے۔ (1) باب صفۃ الصلوۃ کے مسئلہ نمبر ۶ میں گزر گیا ہے کہ قعدہ اخیرہ فرض ہے اب اس کو چھوڑ کر پانچوٹی رکعت کی طرف گیا جو گویا کہ نفل ہوگی اس لئے جب تک پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ نہ کیا ہو اور اس کو مضبوط نہ کیا ہو اس کو چھوڑ کر قعدہ اخیرہ کی طرف آئے اور قعدہ اخیرہ کر کے سلام پھیرے اور سجدہ سہو کرے (۲) پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ کر لیا تو اب جو قعدہ کرے گا وہ نفل نماز کا قعدہ ہوگا اور فرض نماز کا قعدہ اخیرہ چھوٹ گیا اور قاعدہ ہے کہ فرض چھوڑ دے تو نماز فاسد ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس لئے فرض فاسد ہو جائے گا اور نفل بن جائے گا۔ اس لئے اس نماز کو دوبارہ پڑھے (۳) اثر میں ہے عن حماد قال اذا صلى الرجل خمسا ولم يجلس فى الرابعة فانه يزيد السادسة ثم يسلم ثم يستأنف صلوته (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب الرجل یصلی الظهر او العصر خمساج ثانی ص ۳۰۳ نمبر ۳۴۶۱) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ چھٹی رکعت ملالے تا کہ چھ رکعتیں نفل بن جائیں اور فاسد شدہ فرض دوبارہ پڑھے۔ اصول فرض چھوڑنے سے نماز فاسد ہو جائے گی۔ الغی : لغو کر دے۔
And if he forgets the final sitting and stands for a fifth [rak'ah], he returns to the sitting as long as he has not prostrated, cancels the fifth, and performs sajda sahw. (303) (7) If he forgets the final sitting and stands for a fifth rak'ah, he will return to the final sitting as long as he has not prostrated, discard the fifth rak'ah, and perform sajda sahw. (1) It has passed in Chapter Description of Prayer, issue number 6, that the final sitting is fard. So having left it and proceeded to a fifth rak'ah, which is effectively a nafl, as long as he has not prostrated in the fifth rak'ah and strengthened it, he should leave it and return to the final sitting, perform the final sitting and say taslim, and perform sajda sahw. (2) If he has prostrated in the fifth rak'ah, then whatever sitting he does will be a sitting of nafl prayer, and the final sitting of the fard prayer has been missed. The principle is that leaving a fard invalidates the prayer. Therefore, the fard becomes invalid and becomes nafl. So he must repeat the prayer. (3) There is an athar from Hammad: 'If a man prays five [rak'ahs] and does not sit in the fourth, then he should add a sixth, then say taslim, then start his prayer anew.' This athar indicates that he should add a sixth rak'ah so that six rak'ahs become nafl, and then repeat the invalidated fard. Principle: leaving a fard invalidates the prayer. 'al-ghi' means to discard.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage deals with forgetting the final sitting (qada akhir) and mistakenly standing for a fifth rak'ah in a four-rak'ah fard prayer. The ruling is: as long as the worshiper has not prostrated in the fifth rak'ah, he should return to the final sitting, discard the fifth rak'ah as if it never occurred, and then perform sajda sahw at the end. The reasoning is that the final sitting is fard (an integral pillar) in the Hanafi school, and the fifth rak'ah is an extra that is essentially a nafl. Since it has not been 'strengthened' by prostration, it can be cancelled. However, if he has already prostrated in the fifth rak'ah, the prayer becomes invalid because he has missed a fard (the final sitting of the fard prayer). The prayer then transforms into a nafl prayer of five rak'ahs, which is odd and undesirable. To fix this, he should add a sixth rak'ah, making it six rak'ahs of nafl, and then repeat the original fard prayer. This is supported by an athar from Hammad, a tabi'i. The key principle is that leaving a fard invalidates the prayer, but here the Hanafis apply istihsan to salvage it as nafl rather than requiring immediate repetition.

Key Terms
قعدة اخيرة (qada akhir): The final sitting in which tashahhud and salutations are recited before taslim.
لغو (laghw): To cancel or discard; the extra rak'ah is considered null and void.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Return to sitting after prostration and perform sajda sahw.
B) Continue the fifth as nafl and add a sixth rak'ah, then repeat the fard.
C) The prayer is valid as fard with sajda sahw only.
D) Abort the prayer immediately and restart.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, forgetting the final sitting and standing for an extra rak'ah requires returning if no prostration; if prostrated, the prayer becomes nafl and must be completed with an added rak'ah and repeated.
